AGORA GROUP MANAGEMENT DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS
(MD&A) FOR YEAR OF 2019 TO THE FINANCIAL STATEMENTS
REVENUE PLN 1,249.7 MILLION EBITDA PLN 190.2 MILLION
EBITDA EXCL. IFRS 16 PLN 114.8 MILLION NET PROFIT PLN 6.0 MILLION
NET PROFIT EXCL. IFRS 16 PLN 9.6 MILLION OPERATING CASH FLOW PLN 205.5 MILLION OPERATING CASH FLOW EXCL. IFRS 16 PLN 131.5 MILLION
Unless indicated otherwise, all data presented herein represent the period of January ­ December 2019, while comparisons refer to the same period of 2018. All data sources are presented in part IV of this MD&A. A new IFRS 16 standard has been in force since 2019, which influenced the presentation of selected categories of the income statement and balance sheet. In this document the data were presented both with the impact of IFRS 16 on the Group's results and without it.
I. IMPORTANT EVENTS AND FACTORS WHICH INFLUENCE THE FINANCIALS OF THE GROUP [1]
In 2019, the Agora Group (the "Group") generated PLN 1,249.7 million in revenue, an increase by 9.5% yoy. In the fourth quarter of 2019 alone, revenue increased by 9.3% yoy to PLN 378.2 million. In the period from January to December 2019, this figure was most significantly driven by the performance of the cinema business, in which ticket sales increased by 9.1% yoy to PLN 258.1 million, concessions sales increased by 23.1% to PLN 111.0 million and advertising sales in cinemas increased by 17.9% to PLN 35.6 million. The film activity of NEXT FILM recorded an increase in revenue to PLN 42.0 million and this was a record breaking performance in the company's history. There was also an increase in revenue from the food business and operations of the Agora Publishing House ­ by 18.7% yoy to PLN 48.3 million. In the fourth quarter of 2019, revenue in the Movies and Books segment improved by 11.3% yoy to PLN 156.9 million. This is attributable mainly to an increase in revenue from the food business and 23.6% yoy increase in revenue earned by the Agora Publishing House, amounting to PLN 15.7 million. Advertising sales in cinemas increased by 26.0% yoy to PLN 13.1 million, and concession sales grew by 7.7% yoy to PLN 33.7 million. Sales of cinema tickets declined slightly yoy in the last quarter of 2019, amounting to PLN 79.1 million. NEXT FILM's movie activity also had a positive effect on the segment's revenue in the period from October to December 2019. Another important segment that contributed to increased revenue of the Agora Group in 2019 was the Internet segment. In 2019, revenue generated by this segment increased by 17.5% yoy to PLN 209.0 million, and in the fourth quarter of 2019 ­ by 45.6% yoy to PLN 74.7 million. This was the most significant revenue growth recorded by the Group during this period. In both periods, and in particular in the last quarter of 2019, this was mainly driven by the dynamic growth of Yieldbird's revenue. The Outdoor segment's revenue went up by 7.2% yoy to PLN 184.3 million in 2019, and by 8.2% yoy to PLN 55.6 million in the fourth quarter of the year. This was mainly caused by advertisers' higher spending on campaigns implemented with the use of Premium Citylight and Digital panels, including ­ in the period from October to December 2019 ­ on the MoveTV platform. Both in 2019 and in the fourth quarter of 2019, the Press and Radio segments reported a decline in revenue. In the Press segment, it decreased by 10.8% yoy to PLN 254.7 million in 2019, and by 14.6% yoy to PLN 64.1 million in the last quarter of 2019. In July 2019, two out of three printing plants of the Agora Group
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 5

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
were shut down, which significantly contributed to the decrease in revenue from the printing business. In turn, the negative trends on the press advertising market, on the one hand, and the reduction of the portfolio of published press titles, on the other hand, contributed to the decrease in revenues from advertising sales in this segment ­ by 16.6% yoy to PLN 84.8 million in the entire 2019 and by 19.6% yoy to PLN 22.6 million in the fourth quarter of 2019. However, in both periods in question revenue from sales of Gazeta Wyborcza's content increased, as a result of, among other things, the growth in the digital subscription of the daily. It is worth emphasizing another digital success of the Press segment ­ the number of digital subscriptions of Gazeta Wyborcza reached nearly 218 thou. at the end of 2019 and was higher by almost 28.0% yoy. In the Radio segment, revenue decreased by 2.5% yoy to PLN 113.1 million in 2019. In the fourth quarter of 2019, they were only slightly lower yoy and stood at PLN 37.5 million. In both cases, this was mainly due to lower revenue from the sale of third-party airtime and, in 2019 as a whole, also from the sale of airtime at the Group's own radio stations.
In 2019, the Group's operating expenses excluding IFRS 16 increased by 8.1% yoy and amounted to PLN 1,232.3 million. They also increased in the fourth quarter of 2019 ­ by 7.2% yoy to PLN 355.1 million. This growth was driven by a PLN 5.6 million restructuring provision, associated mainly with downsizing of the printing business, and created in the first quarter of 2019, and by impairment losses on assets recognised in the fourth quarter of 2019. In 2019, the operating costs increased the most in the Movies and Books segment. In the fourth quarter of 2019, they increased by 16.7% yoy (to PLN 141.9 million), and in the entire 2019 ­ by 25.5% yoy (to PLN 484.0 million). In both periods under review, the growth was mainly attributable to higher costs of external services, staff costs, as well as the cost of materials and energy consumed and value of goods and materials sold. These cost items increased mainly due to development activities: expansion of the Helios cinema network and growing scale of the food business. Operating costs excluding IFRS 16 increased in the Internet segment as well. The operating costs in this business increased to PLN 70.3 million in the fourth quarter of 2019, and by 20.0% yoy to PLN 194.7 million in 2019. This increase was driven by higher yoy costs of external services related to lease of advertising space, mostly by Yieldbird, in connection with higher advertising revenue. Depreciation costs were also higher yoy. The segment's operating expenses were also affected by write-downs, mainly at Goldenline. The Outdoor segment recorded an increase in operating costs excluding IFRS 16 by 7.6% yoy to PLN 43.7 million in the fourth quarter of 2019, and by 6.6% yoy to PLN 154.4 million over 2019. The development of business in this segment, including in the form of acquisitions, had a decisive influence on the increased level of expenses, translating into higher system maintenance costs, higher promotion and marketing costs and higher costs of execution of marketing campaigns. In the Radio segment, the operating costs in 2019 as a whole increased to PLN 98.9 million, mainly due to higher promotion and marketing costs and staff costs. Yet, in the fourth quarter of 2019 alone, they were lower by 1.3% yoy and amounted to PLN 30.4 million. The decline was mostly due to a lower cost of external services. Operating costs in the Press segment were reduced by 30.1% yoy (to PLN 57.5 million) in the fourth quarter of 2019, resulting in an overall decline by 18.5% yoy to PLN 260.1 million in 2019 as a whole. The decrease was mainly due to the lower costs of materials, energy, goods and printing services, as well as lower staff costs in view of restructuring the printing business and reduced full-time employment.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Agora Group's EBITDA excluding IFRS 16 increased by 14.7% yoy to PLN 54.5 million, and in 2019 as a whole ­ by 16.7% yoy to PLN 114.8 million. At the same time, the Group reported profit at the EBIT level excluding IFRS 16 both in the fourth quarter and in the entire 2019, amounting to, respectively, PLN 23.1 million and PLN 17.4 million. In both periods under review, the Group reported a net profit excluding IFRS 16: PLN 12.2 million in the fourth quarter of 2019 and PLN 9.6 million in 2019 as a whole. The net profit attributable to equity holders of the parent company amounted to PLN 11.5 million in the fourth quarter of 2019, and to PLN 6.9 million in the entire 2019.
The Group's EBITDA presented according to IFRS 16 stood at PLN 190.2 million in 2019 and at PLN 74.8 million in the fourth quarter of 2019. The Group reported profit at the EBIT level both in the fourth quarter and in the entire 2019, amounting to, respectively, PLN 25.1 million and PLN 24.7 million. Net profit amounted to PLN 19.1 million in the fourth quarter of 2019, and PLN 6.0 million in 2019 as a whole.
During the preparation of the financial statements for 2019, Agora carried out impairment tests on assets based on, among others, long-term financial projections of particular segments of the Group. Analyses carried out by the Company demonstrated the necessity to recognise impairment losses on non-current assets. In the fourth quarter of 2019, an impairment loss on assets was recognised in the results of the Internet segment. Its impact on the net profit of Agora S.A. amounts to about PLN 12.7 million and on the consolidated net profit of
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 6

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only the Agora Group ­ to about PLN 6.5 million. However, the impact on the consolidated operating profit at the EBIT level is about PLN 7.4 million in the fourth quarter of 2019 and throughout 2019. It is worth noting that Agora recognised impairment losses on its assets also in 2018. In the fourth quarter of 2018, an impairment loss on assets was also recognised in the Internet segment (amounting to PLN 7.5 million) and in the Press segment (amounting to PLN 2.3 million). Additionally, in the fourth quarter of 2018, the Company recognised an impairment loss on receivables from Ruch S.A. subject to accelerated arrangement proceedings, amounting to PLN 4.0 million. The total effect of impairment losses on the Group's consolidated operating profit for the fourth quarter of 2018 was PLN 14.1 million. In addition, it is worth noting that in 2018 the Group's result on the EBIT level was positively affected by the profit from the sale of real properties in Gdansk and Warsaw in the amount of PLN 13.9 million, and the net profit was affected by the profit from the sale of shares in Stopklatka S.A. in the amount of PLN 26.7 million. On the other hand, the net profit was negatively affected by an impairment loss on overdue receivables from Ruch S.A. exposed to the probability of default in the amount of PLN 20.3 million, impairment loss on GoldenLine's assets in the amount of PLN 6.9 million and impairment loss on magazines in the amount of PLN 2.3 million. As at 31 December 2019, the Group's cash and short-term financial assets amounted to PLN 70.7 million, which comprised of PLN 61.1 million in cash and cash equivalents (cash in hand and at bank and bank deposits) and PLN 9.6 million invested in short-term securities. As at the end of December 2019, the Group's loans and leases amounted to PLN 686.4 million (including lease liabilities under IFRS 16 of PLN 513.9 million).

II. EXTERNAL AND INTERNAL FACTORS IMPORTANT FOR THE DEVELOPMENT OF THE GROUP

1.2 Copy sales of dailies [4]
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the total paid circulation of dailies in Poland decreased by 9.7%, and in the entire 2019 by 10.3%. The largest decrease in both periods was observed in the segment of regional dailies.

1.3 Cinema admissions [10]
The number of tickets sold in Polish cinemas in the fourth quarter of 2019 decreased by 2.2% as compared to the fourth quarter of 2018 and amounted to nearly 18.5 million tickets. This is mainly the result of high popularity of the movie entitled Kler in 2018. In 2019, attendance in cinemas increased by 3.3% compared to 2018, and the number of tickets sold amounted to 61.7 million.
In terms of the data on ticket sales presented by Boxoffice.pl in the fourth quarter of 2019, the number of tickets sold in Helios cinemas amounted to 4.3 million, which means a similar level of sales (a decrease of 0.1%) compared to the fourth quarter of 2018. In 2019, the number of tickets sold in this respect reached 14.0 million, an increase of 10.4% compared to 2018.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the number of tickets sold in Helios cinemas on a calendar basis amounted to 4.3 million, which means a decrease by 4.4% compared to the fourth quarter of 2018. In 2019, the number of tickets sold in this respect reached 14,0 million, an increase of 10.3% compared to 2018.
The upward trend on the cinema market has been going on continuously since 2013, in which the number of tickets sold amounted to 36.3 million. In subsequent years, it amounted to 40.5 million (2014), 44.7 million (2015), 52.0 million (2016), 56.6 million (2017) and 59.7 million (2018).

In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Group's total revenue amounted to PLN 378.2 million and increased by 9.3% yoy.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Agora Group's advertising revenue increased by 13.7% yoy and amounted to PLN 187.9 million. The sharpest growth in advertising revenue was reported in the Internet segment, mainly owing to the activity of Yieldbird. It was also higher in the following segments: the Outdoor segment ­ owing to the expansion of the Premium Citylight and Digital panel portfolio, including acquisition of the MoveTV platform; and in the Movies and Books segment ­ mainly in the Helios cinema network. The Press and Radio segments, however, reported a decline in advertising revenue. It is worth noting that the dynamics of the Press segment's advertising revenue, apart from market trends, were affected by the reduction in titles published. On the other hand, the drop in advertising revenue in the Radio segment was related to lower revenue from the sale of third-party airtime.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, revenue from tickets sold in Helios cinemas decreased by 1.5% yoy and amounted to PLN 79.0 million. In the period under review, 4.3 million tickets were purchased at the Helios cinemas, i.e. 4.4% less than in the fourth quarter of 2018. [10].

[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 10

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Group's copy sales revenue amounted to PLN 37.9 million and increased by 4.7% yoy. This is mainly attributable to higher sales revenues of Agora Publishing House and higher revenues from subscriptions of paid content on Wyborcza.pl. At the end of 2019, the number of digital subscriptions of Gazeta Wyborcza reached nearly 218 thou.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, cinema concession sales increased by 7.7% yoy to PLN 33.7 million. This increase was driven mainly by an increase in average prices in cinema bars.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, revenue from the sales of printing services in the Agora Group were lower yoy and amounted to PLN 10.5 million. This is mainly the effect of shutting down two out of the three printing plants of the Agora Group in mid-2019 and a smaller volume of orders.
Revenue from the movie business increased significantly yoy to PLN 4.0 million. This was related, among other things, to a larger number of new titles in cinema distribution. In the fourth quarter of 2019, NEXT FILM released three Polish productions: a story of a blind pianist inspired by real events ­ Ikar. Legenda Mietka Kosza, a spy thriller ­ The Coldest Game and a documentary about the legendary band Kult ­ Kult. Film. At the same time, cinemas have been screening movies released to the big screen in earlier periods.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, revenue from other sales increased yoy to PLN 25.2 million, mainly due to revenue from the food business and an increase in this revenue item in the Outdoor segment.
In 2019, the Group's total revenue increased by 9.5% yoy and reached PLN 1,249.7 million.
In 2019, the Agora Group's advertising revenue increased by 4.5% yoy and amounted to PLN 579.7 million. They increased significantly (by 20.2% yoy to PLN 187.6 million) in the Internet segment ­ mainly thanks to the dynamic development of Yieldbird, and in the Outdoor segment ­ owing to consistent development of the Premium Citylight and Digital panels, including the purchase of the MoveTV platform panels. Cinemas of the Helios network also reported an increase in advertising revenue ­ to PLN 35.6 million. The sharpest decrease in advertising revenue (by 16.6% yoy to PLN 84.8 million) was reported in the Press segment due to, among other factors, lower sales of advertisement in the paper edition of Gazeta Wyborcza and discontinuation of selected press titles. Advertising revenue of the Radio segment declined by 5.6% yoy to PLN 90.2 million, mainly due to lower sales of advertisements both in third-party ratio stations and in the stations of the Agora Radio Group.
In 2019, revenue from tickets sold in Helios cinemas increased by 9.1% yoy and amounted to PLN 258.0 million. In the period under review, 14.0 million tickets were purchased at the Helios cinemas, i.e. 10.4% more than in 2018. In the same period, the number of cinema tickets sold in Polish cinemas amounted to 61.7 million and increased by 3.3% [10].
In 2019, the Group's copy sales revenue amounted to PLN 139.2 million and increased by 6.2% yoy. This is mainly attributable to good performance of Agora Publishing House and revenues from subscriptions of paid content on Wyborcza.pl. At the end of 2019, the number of digital subscriptions of Gazeta Wyborcza reached nearly 218 thousand.
In 2019, cinema concession sales increased by 23.1% yoy to PLN 111.0 million. This was mainly due to higher cinema attendance and higher average prices at cinema bars.
In 2019, revenue from sales of printing services in the Group amounted to PLN 47.2 million (down by 25.9% yoy). This is mainly due to the shutdown of two out of three printing plants of the Agora Group in July 2019 and lower volume of orders, especially in the coldset technology.
Revenue from the movie business increased significantly yoy to PLN 39.1 million. This was related, among other things, to a larger number of new titles in cinema distribution. In 2019, NEXT FILM released as much as nine Polish productions. At the same time, cinemas continued to screen films introduced to the big screen in earlier periods. In 2019 NEXT FILM started its cooperation with Netflix, under which the platform released 20 film productions to which this company holds distribution rights.
Revenue from other sales amounted to PLN 75.5 million and increased by 37.8% yoy. This increase results primarily from the food business developed within the Movies and Books segment.

In the fourth quarter of 2019, the net operating costs of the Agora Group excluding IFRS 16 increased by 7.2% yoy to PLN 355.1 million. Their increase was reported in the Internet, the Movies and Books and the Outdoor segments. On the other hand, operating costs were lower in the Press segment, which also included the restructured printing activity of the Agora Group starting from the third quarter of 2019, and in the Radio segment.
The largest cost item were costs of external services excluding IFRS 16, which increased by 23.0% yoy to PLN 156.6 million. This cost item increased significantly in the Internet segment, which was driven by higher expenditure on lease of advertising space, mainly by Yieldbird. They were also higher in the Movies and Books segment due to higher costs related to movie and food businesses, rental costs in cinemas and film copy fees. Costs of external services were also higher in the Outdoor segment.
Staff costs reached PLN 89.0 million and were 1.9% higher yoy. The sharpest increase was recorded in the Movies and Books segment, in connection with expansion of the Helios network and development of the food business, as well as in the Outdoor and the Radio segments. Their reduction in other operating segments of the Agora Group was mainly attributable to lower full-time employment.
As at the end of December 2019, the Group's headcount amounted to 2,495 full time employees and decreased by 216 FTEs yoy. This decrease is mainly attributable to lower headcount in the restructured printing and press businesses, as well as support departments. On the other hand, headcount increased in the Movies and Books and the Outdoor segments.
The Group offers various incentive schemes for its employees (for example: cash motivation schemes, incentive schemes in sales departments, incentive schemes for Board Members and key managers, etc.), the costs of which are included in the Group's staff costs.
The year-on-year decrease in the cost of materials and energy consumed, and the value of goods and materials sold was primarily related to the reduction of the Group's printing operations after phasing out the production capacity in two printing plants. This cost category, however, increased in the Movies and Books segment in connection with the development of the food business, printing additional copies of popular books and higher concession sales.
Costs of depreciation and amortisation excluding IFRS 16 increased by 4.8% yoy to PLN 23.8 million. The sharpest increase was recorded in the Movies and Books segment. This was mainly due to the increased number of cinemas in the Helios network, the expansion of the food business and the depreciation of co-producers' contributions in the film business.
The Group's promotion and marketing costs increased by 19.4% yoy to PLN 27.7 million. Their increase was reported in the Movies and Books and the Outdoor segments, whereas the Press, the Internet and the Radio segments reported their decline.
In 2019, the Group's net operating costs excluding IFRS 16 increased by 8.1% yoy to PLN 1,232.3 million.
It is worthy of note that their year-on-year comparability was affected by a number of one-off events. In 2018, an impairment loss on receivables at risk of default in the amount of PLN 20.3 million, a restructuring provision in the amount of PLN 3.6 million, and an impairment loss on assets in the amount of PLN 9.9 million were recognised. On the other hand, the level of Group's operating costs in the first half of 2018 was reduced by the profit on sale of the Company's real properties in Gdask and Warsaw in the amount of PLN 13.9 million recorded in the first quarter of 2018. Total negative impact of those events on the Group's operating results was PLN 19.9 million.
In 2019, the Agora Group's results were burdened with a restructuring provision related mainly to the optimization of the printing business in the amount of PLN 5.6 million and an impairment loss on assets in the amount of PLN 7.5 million. Total negative impact of those events on the Agora Group's results was PLN 13.1 million.
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 13

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
The increase in the Group's operating costs in 2019 was driven by higher operating costs in the Movies and Books, the Internet and the Outdoor segments. However, they decreased in the Radio segment. In 2019, costs of external services excluding IFRS 16 increased by 19.0% yoy to PLN 522.0 million. The increase in this cost item was driven by the Internet, the Movies and Books and the Outdoor segments. In the former, this increase was mainly due to higher costs of lease of advertising space by Yieldbird and resulted from increased advertising revenue. In the second one, it was related to higher costs of film business, rental costs in Helios cinemas, purchase of film copies and development of the food business. The increased costs of external services in the Outdoor segment resulted from higher system maintenance costs. On the other hand, lower costs of external services in the Press segment were the effect of a reduced number of paper copies, i.a. due to discontinuation of some titles, and in the Radio segment -- due to lower costs of purchase of air time in third-party stations and costs of marketing research. In 2019, staff costs increased by 2.3% yoy to PLN 336.2 million. The highest growth was visible in the Movies and Books segment, due to the greater number of cinemas and development of the food business. This cost category was also higher in the Outdoor and the Radio segments. It decreased, however, in the Press and the Internet segments. This cost category was also affected by the restructuring provision associated with downscaling of the printing business. The costs of materials and energy and the value of goods and materials sold amounted to PLN 153.0 million in 2019 and remained relatively flat yoy. This was mainly due to an increase in this cost item in the Movies and Books segment and the Outdoor segment, with a significant reduction in the Press segment in connection with discontinuation of the activity of two printing plants. Costs of depreciation and amortisation excluding IFRS 16 increased by 2.5% yoy to PLN 89.8 million. The sharpest increase was recorded in the Movies and Books and the Internet segments. The increase in the former one was driven by a greater number of Helios cinemas and in the latter one -- by investments in IT infrastructure upgrades, allowing for continued development of advertising products and improvement of visibility of Gazeta.pl in search results of the most popular search engines. A slight increase in costs of depreciation and amortisation was also recorded in the Radio segment. In turn, the Press and the Outdoor segments reported a decline in this cost item. Promotion and marketing costs increased in the period under review, amounting to PLN 77.5 million. They were higher in the Movies and Books, the Radio and the Outdoor segments. However, they were reduced in the Internet and the Press segments. In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Group's net operating costs, reported in accordance with IFRS 16, amounted to PLN 353.1 million, and in 2019 as a whole ­ to PLN 1,225.0 million.

translation only
3. PROSPECTS
In July 2019, two out of three printing plants owned by the Agora Group were shut down. The Company conducted group layoffs and the provision related to employment restructuring in Agora S.A. and Agora Poligrafia Sp. z o.o. in the amount of PLN 5.6 million was recognized in the financial result of the Company and the Agora Group in the first quarter of 2019. Therefore, the scale of printing activities in 2020 will be significantly smaller than in 2019. In the future, the Company plans to dispose of real property that has been used for printing operations, however, this may not happen in 2020.
In 2020, for the first time, both operating revenue and costs of the Group will be visibly affected by the food business, which the Helios Group started as early as in 2018 and has been expanding in 2019 through Foodio Concepts Sp. z o.o. and Step Inside Sp. z o.o. It is the goal of the Company's Management Board that the results of the food business in 2020 should be significantly higher than in 2019.
At the same time, in 2019 the Agora Group made a number of investments.
In February 2019, Agora acquired a 40% stake in the capital group of Eurozet Sp. z o.o., and in September 2019 the Management Board of Agora decided to purchase remaining 60% of shares in Eurozet Sp. z o.o. The condition of this acquisition is obtaining the consent of the President of the Office of Competition and Consumer Protection. Agora submitted an appropriate application in this respect on October 28, 2019. The consent of the President of the Office of Competition and Consumer Protection for the concentration and exercise of the option to purchase 60% shares in Eurozet will significantly affect the financial performance, level of investments in other businesses and the structure of the Agora Group.
In July 2019, AMS S.A. from the Agora Group acquired 60% of shares in Piano Group sp. z o.o. with its registered office in Warsaw. Consolidation of this company's figures will have a positive effect on the performance of the Outdoor segment and the entire Agora Group.
In September 2019, Agora became the majority shareholder of HRlink Sp. z o.o., holding 79.8% of its share capital. The full consolidation of HRlink Sp. z o.o.'s figures will affect the results of the Internet segment and the entire Agora Group.
On March 11, 2020, the World Health Organization assessed that the Covid-19 epidemic could be characterized as a pandemic. At present, it is difficult to predict the further development of the related situation and estimate the scale of its negative impact on economic growth in Poland and Europe, as well as the related tendency of advertisers to promote their products and services. As part of the fight against the epidemic, the Polish authorities issued a regulation pursuant to which from 12 to 25 March 2020 all educational and cultural institutions, including cinemas, were closed. In the Company's opinion, closing the Helios network cinemas for a period of 2 weeks will not have a significant impact on the results of the Agora Group in 2020. It is also difficult to predict how the situation will look after these two weeks, and therefore its impact on the condition of the industry and Agora Group's results cannot be assessed.
3.1 Revenue
3.1.1 Advertising market [3]
The advertising market in Poland in the fourth quarter of 2019 increased by 4.0%. Advertisers spent over PLN 2.9 billion promoting their products and services during this time. Throughout 2019, the value of advertising spending increased by 3.0% to PLN 9.8 billion.
The company decided not to provide an estimate at this stage of the increase in advertising expenditure in Poland in 2020 due to the spread of the coronavirus epidemic and the difficulty in estimating its impact on the economic growth and advertising market in Poland this year. Any estimates will be provided by the Company at a later date.
3.1.2 Copy sales
In 2020, negative trends regarding the decline in copy sales of newspapers and magazines in the printed form will persist. Their dynamics partly depends also on the condition of the Polish press distribution market. In addition, the Company systematically reviews the portfolio of press titles, which may be reflected in both the number of copies sold and the copy sales revenue. In 2019, the Company decided to cease publishing the titles of Opiekun and Kuchnia regularly. At the same time, the Company is working on the development of sales of digital
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 15

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
publications. At the end of December 2019, the number of paid digital subscriptions to Gazeta Wyborcza amounted to nearly 218 thou., and the share of revenues from the sale of digital subscriptions to the newspaper was 24.0%.
3.1.3 Ticket sales
The most important factors affecting the turnout in Polish cinemas are the repertoire, weather, wealth of Polish society and distance to the cinema. The available information shows that the number of tickets sold in Polish cinemas in 2019 amounted to 61.7 million, which means an increase of 3.3% compared to 2018 [10]. The available movie repertoire for 2020 allowed the Company to assume that in the entire 2020 turnout in cinemas will be at a similar level to that recorded in 2019.
However, at the beginning of March 2020, price competition of cinema network operators in Poland intensified. After announcing a price change by one of the competitors, the Helios cinema network decided to introduce a uniform ticket price in all their multiplexes. This kind of competition can affect the level of turnover in cinemas, and ultimately even change the business model of cinema operations in the long run. At the moment, however, it is not possible to estimate the effect this change will bring to the cinema market or Helios cinema network.
On March 11, 2020, the World Health Organization assessed that the Covid-19 epidemic could be characterized as a pandemic. At present, it is difficult to predict the further development of the related situation and estimate the scale of its negative impact on economic growth in Poland and Europe, as well as the related tendency of advertisers to promote their products and services. As part of the fight against the epidemic, the Polish authorities issued a regulation pursuant to which from 12 to 25 March 2020 all educational and cultural institutions, including cinemas, were closed. In the Company's opinion, closing the Helios cinemas for a period of 2 weeks will not have a significant impact on the results of the Agora Group in 2020. It is also difficult to predict what the situation will look like after these two weeks, therefore it cannot be assessed on the condition of the industry in Poland and results of the Agora Group.
3.2 Operating cost
In 2020, the Movies and Books segment will have the greatest impact on the level of operating costs of the Agora Group, in particular due to the development of the Helios cinema network and gastronomic network, mainly under the Pasibus brand.
On the other hand, the operating costs of the Press segment will be significantly lower than in previous years, mainly due to the optimization of printing operations carried out in 2019 and the closing of two out of the three printing plants belonging to the Agora Group in July 2019.
3.2.1 Costs of external services
The cost of external services in 2020 will largely depend on the cost of payment for film copies directly related to the level of revenues from ticket sales and the EUR to PLN exchange rate. The increase in this cost item will be additionally affected by: the opening of new cinema facilities in 2020, the development of gastronomic activities, the cost of leasing advertising space in the Outdoor advertising segment, the activities of Agora Publishing House and the implementation of other development projects.
3.2.2 Staff cost
According to the Company's estimates, in 2020 the costs of salaries and employee benefits will be at a higher level than in 2019. The largest increase in this cost item will take place in the Movies and Books segment due to the development of the gastronomic business and opening of new cinema facilities. An increase in the minimum rate per hour of work from PLN 14.7 to PLN 17.0 in 2020 will also have a significant impact, in particular on the Helios cinema network. An increase in the costs of remuneration and benefits was also planned in the Internet segment and in supporting divisions. In the Outdoor Advertising and Radio segments, they should not be significantly higher than those recorded in 2019. This cost item will be reduced in the Press segment as a result of lower full-time employment and the closing of two out of the three Agora Group printing plants, which was associated with group layoffs in 2019.
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 16

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
3.2.3 Promotion and marketing cost
In 2020, Agora Group is planning to implement more development activities, which include promotional activities. The dynamics of changes in individual media, the number of launched development projects as well as market activities of the Group's competitors may affect the level of these expenses. Considering the above factors, the Company estimates that in 2020 this cost item may decrease yoy.
3.2.4 Cost of raw materials and energy
In 2020, the optimization of the printing activities and reduction of the volume of printed titles will have a significant impact on this cost item. In the Company's opinion, it will be significantly lower in the entire Group than in 2019.
The increase in this cost item will be seen in the Movies and Books segment, which is mainly related to the development of cinema operations.
4. THE GROWTH DIRECTIONS OF THE AGORA GROUP
The primary objective of the Company's Management Board is to accelerate the development and increase the scale of operations of the Agora Group. The new strategy of the Agora Group for the years 2018-2022 is based on the following pillars:
· systematic development of the existing businesses, including through acquisitions strengthening current businesses of the Agora Group,
· extending the offer of the largest enterprises with innovative products or premium services, · development of a new business in prospective market segments.
In February 2019, the Company acquired 40% of shares in Eurozet Sp. z o.o., the second largest Polish broadcaster in terms of radio coverage. In October 2019, Agora applied to the President of the Office of Competition and Consumer Protection for consent to acquire the remaining 60% of shares in Eurozet. This transaction may change the Agora Group's position on the radio broadcasters' market and may affect the verification of the Group's investment plans in non-media businesses. At the same time, it is worth noting that this potential transaction does not change the key objectives and strategic goals of the Agora Group. Acceleration of growth and increase in the scale of the Agora Group's activities remains the most important goal, which will be reflected in increased revenue and profitability of the Group.
Taking into account the application for the consent of the President of the Office of Competition and Consumer Protection for the acquisition of 60% of shares in Eurozet Sp. z o.o. and the investments already made in the area of Internet and digital outdoor activities, the Company will engage in a smaller number of new investment projects by 2022.
The cinemas remain the priority development direction of the Agora Group in the area of entertainment in the broad sense. To date, the Company has not been able to find other projects in this area that would provide the Group with an equally satisfactory rate of return, whilst offering good development prospects.
The food business developed within the Helios Group by Foodio Concepts Sp. z o.o. and Step Inside Sp. z o.o. completed the first stage of its operation. At the end of 2019, the first company operated as many as 14 restaurants. The goal for the coming year is to improve their financial efficiency. The second concept ­ developed under the Pasibus brand name ­ had 6 operating restaurants at the end of last year. At the beginning of 2020, an investment agreement was signed, which will ensure faster development of this promising burger chain.
Another important directions of development in the strategic perspective of the Agora Group until 2022 are digitalization and further development of premium services and products. We are still looking for assets that would complement or strengthen our portfolio in these areas. Examples of such investments include Piano Group Sp. z o.o., the owner of the Move TV platform. With this investment, AMS has taken another step in building its digital media and services offer and strengthened its position in the promising DOOH area.
An example of measures related to the expansion of significant projects of the Group by innovative products or premium services is the continued dynamic development of Yieldbird, the leader in the ad-tech industry, related to
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 17

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only the introduction of a product sold in the SaaS (software as a service) model to its offer. Yieldbird has so far achieved global success with its business and continues to grow in foreign markets. We have also made investments in the B2B solutions segment. In June 2019, we acquired further shares in ROI Hunter, a Czech company, and we hold a 23.9% stake in this entity. ROI Hunter is a provider of a marketing platform which allows companies from the e-commerce industry to promote and sell products via Google and Facebook. In September, we also became the majority shareholder of HRlink Sp. z o.o., one of the fastest growing technology companies in Europe. The sale of high-quality content in the subscription model remains an important direction of Agora's development. During the current strategic perspective, the Group wants to triple the average number of subscriptions of Gazeta Wyborcza and podcasts of Radio TOK FM, as well as ensure improved monetization of this business model. Ultimately in the year 2022, half of the revenues of Gazeta Wyborcza is to be generated from digital sources and its profitability is expected to improve regularly. The Company is working steadily to achieve this objective. At the end of 2019, the number of digital subscriptions of Gazeta Wyborcza reached a record level of nearly 218 thousand and the share of digital revenues of Gazeta Wyborcza in total revenue of the daily increased to 24.0%. The number of sold subscriptions of Radio TOK FM podcasts has also increased ­ at the end of December 2019, it reached over 20 thou.
5. INFORMATION ON CURRENT AND EXPECTED FINANCIAL SITUATION OF THE GROUP
The Management Board of Agora S.A. is of the opinion that current and expected financial situation of the Group is stable and its financial liquitidy is not threatened. The detailed description of the Group's financial situation and its financial results are presented in the section III of this Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019.

(1) the amounts do not include revenues and total cost of cross-promotion of Agora's different media if such promotion is executed without prior reservation between segments of the Agora Group; the direct variable cost of campaigns carried out on advertising panels is the only cost that is included above; it is allocated from the Outdoor segment to other segments; (2) based on invoices booked in the period, the amount in the Movies and Books segment includes also PLN 32.2 million of property, plant and equipment in finance lease; (3) reconciling positions show data not included in particular segments, i.a.: other revenues and costs of Agora's supporting divisions (centralized IT, administrative, finance and HR functions, etc., excluding costs of office space in the Company`s headquarters, which are allocated to segments), the Management Board of Agora S.A., Agora TC Sp. z o.o. and Agora Finanse Sp. z o.o., intercompany eliminations and other matching adjustments, which reconcile the data presented in the management reports to the consolidated financials of the Agora Group.
2.3. Sales and markets
Over 85.0% of the total sales of the Group were related to sales in domestic market. Sales to foreign markets are realized mainly through the sales of printing and advertising services to foreign customers and sales of publications (including foreign subscriptions). The Group does not depend on one particular customer. The biggest customers of the Group (in respect of the turnover) are press distributors and Google (companies unrelated to Agora S.A.). In 2019, the value of transactions with none of the distributors exceeded 10.0% of the Group's total revenues.
2.4. Suppliers
The Group does not depend on one particular supplier. Newsprint, printing services and film copy purchase are important cost items of the Group. Newsprint used for printing services for external customers and in order to print the Group's own titles is purchased from several suppliers. In 2019, the value of transactions with none of the suppliers exceeded 10.0% of the Group's total revenues.
2.5. Finance cost, net
Net financial activities of the Group for 2019 were influenced mainly by costs of commissions and interest on bank loans and finance lease liabilities (including interest expenses on leasing liabilities recognized in accordance with IFRS 16 in amount of PLN 15.7 million) and revaluation of put option liabilities. Significant impact on finance income had remeasurement of equity interest at the acquisition date related to the acquisition of HRlink Sp. z o.o. (formerly: Online Technologies HR Sp. z o.o.) in the third quarter of 2019 in amount of PLN 7.0 million. Moreover, the Group received income from its cash investments and the foreign exchange gains.

3.1. Non-current assets
The increase in non-current assets, versus 31 December 2018 results mainly from the recognition of the new rightof-use assets in accordance with IFRS 16 in the amount of PLN 507.3 million (after including reclassification of property, plant and equipment in finance lease and prepaid administrative decisions for constructing advertising panels in the road lane, the total carrying amount of right-of-use assets as at 31 December 2019 amounted to PLN 590.4 million) and increase in investment in associates accounted for the equity method (including the acquisition of 40.0% shares in Eurozet Sp. z o.o., which purchase price with transaction costs amounted to PLN 137.2 million and additional acquisition of shares in ROI Hunter a.s., which purchase price amounted to PLN 9.5 million).
The increase in non-current assets results mainly from the increase of intangible assets (including recognition of goodwill in the total amount of PLN 25.1 million) due to accounting for the acquisition of the subsidiaries of Piano Group Sp. z o.o. and HRlink Sp. z o.o. (formerly: Online Technologies HR Sp. z o.o.). In the discussed period, the Group also incurred capital expenditure on property, plant and equipment and intangible assets, which to some extent were compensated by depreciation charges for assets.
3.2. Current assets
The decrease in current assets, versus 31 December 2018, stems mainly from the decrease in short-term financial assets and inventories. Simultaneuosly, the Group recorded an increase in cash during this period.
The increase in current asset, versus 30 September 2019, stems mainly from the increase in trade receivables and cash.

[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 23

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
3.3. Non-current liabilities and provisions
The increase in non-current liabilities and provisions compared to 31 December 2018, stems mainly from the increase in long-term bank loans (including the transfer of loan tranche in the first quarter of 2019 by Agora S.A. in the amount of PLN 75.0 million due to the purchase of shares in Eurozet Sp z o.o.), an increase in lease liabilities regarding right-of-use assets in accordance with IFRS 16. Moreover, the increase of non-current liabilities resulted from the recognition of put option liabilities granted to non-controlling shareholders of Piano Group Sp. z o.o. and HRlink Sp. z o.o. (formerly: Online Technologies HR Sp. z o.o.) in the total amount of PLN 16.0 million, and due to revaluation of liabilities due to put option granted to shareholders/non-controlling shareholders of Helios S.A
The increase in non-current liabilities and provisions compared to 30 September 2019, stems mainly from the increase of lease liabilities due to recognition of the new lease liabilities and put option liabilities. Meanwhile, noncurrent liabilities from bank loans decreased in connection with their reclassification to current liabilities and deferred tax liabilities decrease.
3.4. Current liabilities and provisions
The increase in current liabilities and provisions, versus 31 December 2018, stems mainly from the increase in lease liabilities related to recognition of the lease liabilities in accordance with IFRS 16, increase in short-term bank loans and trade payables.
The increase in current liabilities and provisions, versus 30 September 2019, stems mainly from the increase in trade payables and acquisition of property, plant and equipment and increase in accruals, partially offset by reduction of bank loans.

4.1. Operating activities
The cash flows from operating activities, in 2019, were higher comparing to the level recorded in the prior year. The transfer of rental payments under lease agreements recognised in the balance sheet in accordance with IFRS 16 to cash flows from financing activities had significant impact on a higher level of cash flows from operating activities.
4.2. Investment activities
Negative net cashflows from investing activities, in 2019, result mainly from expenditure on the purchase of shares in associates: Eurozet Sp. z o.o, ROI Hunter a.s. and subsidiaries: Piano Group Sp. z o.o. and HRlink Sp. z o. o. (formerly: Online Technologies HR Sp. z o.o.) as well as expenditure on property, plant and equipment and intangible assets. Those outflows were, to some extent, compensated by net inflows from disposal of short-term securities and proceeds from sale of property, plant and equipment.
4.3. Financing activities
Negative net cashflows from financing activities in 2019, stems mainly from the expenditure on repayment of loan and lease liabilities (including the payment of lease liabilities recognised under IFRS 16) and payment of dividend. The above inflows were to some extent, compensated by loans inflows (including the transfer of loan tranche by Agora S.A. in the amount of PLN 75.0 million in connection with the acquisition of shares in Eurozet Sp. z o. o.).

translation only
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the result of the Movies and Books segment at the EBIT level excluding IFRS 16 was lower by 22.7% yoy and amounted to PLN 15.0 million. The segment's EBITDA excluding IFRS 16 also decreased ­ by 8.6% yoy to PLN 24.5 million. Such performance of the segment was mainly affected by the loss related to the development of the food business and loss recorded due to movie business in the fourth quarter of 2019.
In 2019, the result of the Movies and Books segment at the EBIT level excluding IFRS 16 increased by 12.3% yoy to PLN 37.5 million. The segment's EBITDA excluding IFRS 16 also increased ­ by 11.9% yoy to PLN 71.2 million. Activities performed by the majority of the businesses in the segment had a positive effect on this performance. The segment's results were adversely affected only by the food business developed by Foodio Concepts and Step Inside. This was primarily due to the fact that in the current, initial, phase of this project's development, the costs associated with launching consecutive restaurants exceed the revenue generated by the business. In 2019, loss on the food business at the EBIT and EBITDA level stood at, respectively, PLN 10.1 million and PLN 9.0 million.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, according to IFRS 16, the Movies and Books segment recorded a profit at the EBIT level of PLN 16.4 million. In 2019 as a whole, the segment's EBIT reported in accordance with IFRS 16 stood at PLN 43.0 million. In the corresponding periods, , the segment's EBITDA came in at PLN 39.0 million and PLN 128.2 million, respectively.
Figures presented in accordance with IFRS 16 are not comparable to figures for 2018. In the fourth quarter and throughout 2019, in accordance with IFRS 16, the costs of agreements for the lease of space, both in the Helios cinemas and the Foodio Concepts facilities, have not been recognised in the presented segment's results under external services, where they had been presented before. They formed the basis for the recognition of a noncurrent asset (due to the right to use space) which depreciated and affects the growth of this cost item in the segment. At the same time, in view of recognized liabilities under long-term lease agreements, interest expenses included in financial expenses are recognized in the income statement. This method of recognition of expenses improves the presented operating profits, in particular at the EBITDA level, due to the increase in depreciation. Reclassification of lease agreements also has a positive effect on the EBIT figure.
1. REVENUE [3]
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the revenue of the Movies and Books segment increased by 11.3% yoy to PLN 156.9 million.
To the greatest extent, this increase was driven by higher revenue from the food business, the scale of which was negligible in the corresponding period of 2018. Revenues from cinema operations have also increased, mainly driven by higher advertising and concession sales in cinemas, with a slight decrease in ticket sales. The increase in advertising sales in cinemas resulted from the implementation of advertising campaigns for new customers and a larger number of campaigns settled in the form of barter, while the increased revenue from concession sales was reported owing to increased average prices in cinema bars. Revenues from tickets sold in the Helios cinema network declined by 1.4% (as compared to the fourth quarter of 2018) to PLN 79.1 million. Both in the fourth quarter of 2019 and in 2019 as a whole, the dynamics of the number of tickets sold in Helios cinemas was significantly higher than the market.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the revenue of Agora Publishing House amounted to PLN 15.7 million and increased by 23.6% yoy, mainly as a result of higher revenues from book sales. In that period, Agora Publishing House sold approximately 0.5 million books as well as film and music publications. The increase in the Agora Publishing House's revenues in the period in question was significantly affected by the commercial success of Szczerze by Donald Tusk. Other bestselling titles included: Kolejne 365 dni by Blanka Lipiska, Pieklo mnie nie chcialo ­ a biography of Krzysztof Wielicki, Becoming ­ Michelle Obama's memoir, and Syn Miasta ­ an album by Muniek Staszczyk.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Movies and Books segment's total revenue from film co-production and distribution amounted to PLN 4.9 million, showing an increase yoy. That was due to, among other factors, more new titles distributed in cinemas. In the fourth quarter of 2019, NEXT FILM released three Polish productions: a story of a blind pianist inspired by real events ­ Ikar. Legenda Mietka Kosza, a spy thriller ­ The Coldest Game and a documentary about the legendary band Kult ­ Kult. Film. At the same time, cinemas continued to screen features released to the big screen in earlier periods.
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 28

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
In 2019, the revenue of the Movies and Books segment increased by 24.4% yoy to PLN 521.5 million. This is a result of an increase in revenues of all business lines in this segment. The increase in the segment's revenues in 2019 was mainly driven by higher revenues from the movie business generated by NEXT FILM.
In 2019, the Movies and Books segment's total revenue from film co-production and distribution amounted to PLN 42.0 million, showing a considerable increase yoy. In 2019, NEXT FILM released 9 Polish productions: action movie Underdog, sequel of the iconic film series Kogel Mogel ­ Miszmasz, czyli Kogel Mogel 3 (watched at cinemas by nearly 2.4 million viewers), romantic comedy Cale szczescie, drama Slodki koniec dnia, crime comedy Na bank sie uda, historical drama Pilsudski, a story of a blind pianist inspired by real events Ikar. Legenda Mietka Kosza, a spy thriller The Coldest Game and a documentary about the legendary band Kult ­ Kult. Film. At the same time, cinemas continued to screen features released to the big screen in earlier periods. In 2019 NEXT FILM started its cooperation with Netflix, under which the platform released 20 film productions to which the Agora Group's company holds distribution rights.
In 2019, revenue from tickets sold in Helios cinemas amounted to PLN 258.1 million, showing an increase by 9.1% yoy. A contributing factor was higher number of viewers (by 10.3% yoy) in Helios cinemas which translated into 14.0 million tickets sold. Concession sales amounted to PLN 111.0 million and increased by 23.1% yoy, driven by higher cinema attendance. Revenue from advertising sales in Helios cinemas also increased and stood at PLN 35.6 million.
In 2019, the revenue of Agora Publishing House amounted to PLN 48.3 million and increased by 18.7% yoy as a result of higher book sales. In that period, Agora Publishing House sold approximately 1.4 million books as well as film and music publications. The bestselling titles included: Kolejne 365 dni by Blanka Lipiska, Becoming ­ Michelle Obama's memoir, Sodoma by Frédéric Martel, Szczerze by Donald Tusk, biography Czapkins. Historia Tomka Mackiewicza, Fisz Emade Tworzywo's Radar CD and Kamerdyner DVD.
2. COST
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the operating costs of the Movies and Books segment excluding the effect of IFRS 16 increased by 16.7% yoy and amounted to PLN 141.9 million.
The increase in the costs, according to this presentation, resulted primarily from 26.1% yoy increase in staff costs which were reported at PLN 22.7 million. The increase was attributable mostly to a higher headcount ­ due to a greater number of Helios cinemas, an increase in the minimum hourly wage from PLN 13.7 to PLN 14.7, and development of operations in the food business.
Expenditure on external services increased by 7.5% yoy to PLN 66.3 million. This increase was mainly driven by the increase in rental costs related to restaurants and Helios cinemas, and the settlement of costs related to the release of new titles by NEXT FILM.
An increase in the cost of materials and energy consumed and the cost of goods and materials sold by 27.4% to PLN 14.4 million was attributable to the expansion of operations in the food business, higher concession sales in cinema bars and addition of new facilities to the Helios cinema network.
Promotion and marketing costs also increased, amounting to PLN 10.1 million. This was mainly driven by higher expenditure on promotion in the area of film distribution ­ both with respect to films released in the fourth quarter of 2019 and those that premiered in the first quarter of 2020.
The segment's depreciation costs were also higher yoy and amounted to PLN 9.3 million in the fourth quarter of 2019. This was related to increased depreciation of co-producers' contributions to films and the expansion of the food business and the Helios cinema network.
Operating costs of Agora Publishing House went up by 23.6% yoy and reached PLN 15.2 million. Their increase was associated with higher expenditure on the promotion of the Publishing House's selected products, higher revenue from book sales and the expansion of the music business.
In 2019, operating costs of the Movies and Books segment excluding IFRS 16 increased by 25.5% yoy and stood at PLN 484.0 million.
The increase in the segment's operating costs excluding the impact of IFRS 16, resulted from higher costs of external services (up by 23.9% yoy to PLN 237.7 million). The increase was primarily attributable to higher
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 29

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
payments to film producers with respect to film business, higher rental costs for Helios cinemas and food business, and higher costs of film copy purchases due to higher ticket sales.
The staff costs also increased ­ by 31.4% yoy to PLN 74.4 million. This increase was attributable mostly to a higher headcount ­ due to increased number of Helios cinemas, an increase in the minimum hourly wage from PLN 13.7 to PLN 14.7, and to the development of operations in the food business.
As a result of development of operations in the food business, higher concession sales and increase in the number of the Helios cinemas, a 38.6% increase (to PLN 49.9 million) was recorded in the costs of materials and energy consumed and in the cost of goods and materials sold. There was also an increase in depreciation costs which amounted to PLN 33.2 million, mainly due to the expansion of the Helios cinema network and development of operations in the food business.
Promotion and marketing costs also increased to PLN 30.8 million. That was mainly driven by increased expenditure on promotion in the area of film distribution (related to a higher number of movies released as compared to 2018) and on cinema advertising.
Operating costs of Agora Publishing House went up by 16.3% yoy and reached PLN 46.4 million. This increase was related to, among other factors, higher revenue from book sales and the expansion of the music business.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, operating costs of the Movies and Books segment, presented in accordance with IFRS 16, amounted to PLN 140.5 million. The implementation of this standard had the greatest impact on the recognition of costs of external services and depreciation.
Over 2019, operating costs of the Movies and Books segment, presented in accordance with IFRS 16, reached PLN 478.5 million. The implementation of this standard had the greatest impact on the recognition of costs of external services and depreciation.
3. NEW INITIATIVES
The Helios cinema network finished 2019 with three new facilities. In the fourth quarter of 2019, it was expanded by another, 49th multiplex, located in Galeria Gondola in Legionowo. This cinema, opened on 6 December, houses four screening rooms for more than 600 viewers and has been equipped with state-of-the-art technological solutions to ensure unforgettable cinema emotions. Earlier in 2019, Helios opened cinemas in the Blue City shopping centre in Warsaw and in the Tkalnia shopping and entertainment centre in Pabianice. In addition, in the two existing multiplexes, the Helios network offered its viewers the possibility of watching movies in the Helios Dream screening rooms. Since the end of October 2019, one such screening room is also operating at the Helios cinema in the Sukcesja Shopping Centre in Lodz and soon there will be another one, and since 6 December 2019, customers of the Posnania Shopping Centre in Poznan may enjoy movies in two Helios Dream rooms as well. In total, at the end of 2019 the network had 13 Helios Dream screening rooms, promoted by the slogan Wymarzone miejsce na film (A dream place for a movie). All of them are equipped with comfortable recliner seats and technological solutions that ensure exceptional image and sound quality. The unique Helios Dream concept is the answer to the cinema fans' wish for a comfortable space for watching movies.
Apart from movies from the current repertoire, the Helios cinema network has once again arranged special screenings for its viewers. In the fourth quarter of 2019, Helios's multiplexes featured, among others, selected episodes of Przyjaciele (Friends) to celebrate the 25th anniversary of the premiere of this comedy series of all time, as well as the first episodes of the new seasons of Wataha (The Pack) and Wikingowie (Vikings). Ukrainianspeaking viewers had the opportunity to watch the Joker movie, and the participants of the Co Jest Grane 24 poleca w Kinie Konesera (Co Jest Grane 24 recommends in Conneisseur Cinema) cycle could watch Serce Jamajki (Inna De Yard: The Soul of Jamaica) and Krewetki w cekinach (The Shiny Shrimps) in the Warsaw multiplex. Throughout 2019, Helios's cinemas have been inviting viewers to such special screenings, including football match broadcasts and screenings from the Kultura Dostpna (Culture Available) series. A unique project carried out in August and September 2019 were the tournaments and broadcasts of competitions between amateurs and professionals in computer games. E-sport fans were invited to Helios cinemas in Gdansk and Warsaw. On 15 December 2019, the Cinema Day was celebrated all over Poland - the Helios network once again was involved in this initiative organized by the largest operators, in which studio cinemas were also engaged. On that day, the prices of tickets for all screenings cost only 12 PLN.
In October 2019, NEXT FILM from the Helios group released Ikar. Legenda Mietka Kosza, a movie directed by Maciej Pieprzyca. This is the story of a legend of Polish jazz, a rebel, an outsider, a blind piano genius. In the movie,

NEXT FILM was a distributor and co-producer of this movie. Since the beginning of November, viewers could watch the long-awaited film The Coldest Game by Lukasz Komicki. The most recent production of Watchout Studio, distributed by NEXT FILM, has featured international and Polish stars: Bill Pullman, Robert Wickiewicz, Lotte Verbeek, James Bloor and Alexei Sieriebriakow. Earlier in 2019, NEXT FILM released the following titles: Underdog starring Eryk Lubos and Mamed Khalidov, another part of the popular comedy Miszmasz czyli Kogel Mogel 3, the romantic comedy Cale szczcie, Slodki koniec dnia ­ a movie awarded at the Sundance Festival, starring Krystyna Janda, a crime comedy Na bank si uda and a historical drama, Pilsudski. The productions distributed by NEXT FILM in 2019 met not only with the interest of viewers, but also with the recognition of the Polish film industry, receiving a total of 22 nominations for Eagles Polish Film Awards. The legend of Mietek Kosz for Best Music (Leszek Mozdzer) and Best Sound (Marcin Pawlowski, Robert Czyzewicz), and Robert Wickiewicz was awarded for the best supporting male role in the film The Coldest Game. It is also worth mentioning that since March 2019, NEXT FILM has been cooperating with Netflix, and more than 20 films that have been co-produced and distributed by the company have been gradually introduced to the platform, including Pokot (Spoor), an award-winning movie directed by Agnieszka Holland and Kasia Adamik. This complements the existing NEXT FILM distribution channels.
The food business is also dynamically growing in the Helios capital group. In March, Helios signed a letter of intent regarding cooperation with some partners of Food for Nation, the owner of Pasibus burger restaurants, while in April, it obtained a consent of the Office of Competition and Consumer Protection for developing the abovementioned business. As a result, since May new Pasibus burger restaurants have been opened together with Helios. In the last months of 2019, restaurants under this brand were opened in Lublin and Czestochowa. This is the fifth and sixth burger restaurant opened in cooperation with Helios; in total, about several dozen of such facilities are to be established. Foodio Concepts, a subsidiary of Helios, which develops restaurants under the brands of Papa Diego and Van Dog, has also been expanding its operations. Since the fourth quarter of 2019, amateurs of Mexican cuisine may enjoy it in the newly opened Papa Diego restaurants in Szczecin and Gdynia. In total, at the end of 2019 Papa Diego's restaurants operated in 13 cities, including Gdansk, Katowice, Opole, Poznan and Warsaw.
At the end of 2019, the Agora Publishing House offered an exceptionally large number of attractive new releases to its readers, listeners and viewers. The readers were particularly interested in the personal journal of the President of the European Council, Donald Tusk, entitled Szczerze. It was released on 12 December 2019, but made its way to the top of the bestseller lists already in the pre-sale period. Pieklo mnie nie chcialo, a biography of Krzysztof Wielicki, a legend of Polish Himalayan mountaineering, and Milo zaczyna si od miloci, a unique, tastefully edited collection of Kora's notes compiled by Kamil Sipowicz, also enjoyed great interest among readers.
For music fans, Agora offered, among others, Syn miasta ­ a solo album by Muniek Staszczyk, well received by critics, Plyta z zadr w sercu ­ a second album by Jazz Band Mlynarski-Masecki, as well as the project entitled MTV Unplugged Kasia Kowalska.
The most popular of the new releases of the Agora Publishing House in 2019 included, among others, a book that became a global phenomenon ­ Becoming, an intimate autobiography of former First Lady of the United States, Michelle Obama. We are proud to have become its publisher in Poland. The list of bestsellers also included Kolejne 365 dni by Blanka Lipiska and the acclaimed In the Closet of the Vatican: Power, Homosexuality, Hypocrisy by Frederic Martel, as well as Czapkins by Dominik Szczepaski ­ a biography of Tomek Mackiewicz who died tragically during his descent from Nanga Parbat. All these books were listed for many weeks as bestsellers by Empik, the largest book distributor in Poland. Music fans, on the other hand, enjoyed the latest albums of Pro8L3M, Fisz Emade, and Kwiat Jabloni ­ the best debut of the year, according to many music reviewers.
In October 2019 Agora Publishing House, as the first book publisher in Poland, launched POCZYTAWSZY, a podcast on the latest book releases.
