Both in the fourth quarter of 2019 and in the entire 2019, the Press segment's operating result increased yoy. In the fourth quarter of 2019, EBIT excluding IFRS 16 reached PLN 6.6 million, whereas in the corresponding period of 2018, the segment incurred an operating loss. For the entire 2019, the loss at the EBIT level decreased significantly yoy and amounted to PLN 5.4 million. However, the Press segment reported positive EBITDA both in the fourth quarter and in the entire 2019, amounting to, respectively, PLN 7.7 million and PLN 2.1 million. It is worth noting that the comparability of data was affected by the recognition of impairment losses on receivables from RUCH S.A. in 2018, in the amount of PLN 20.3 million, as well as recognition of impairment losses related to selected magazines in the amount of PLN 2.3 million.
The implementation of IFRS 16 had no significant effect on the recognition of the operating costs in the Press segment or the segment's operating results.
1. REVENUE
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Press segment's total revenue decreased by 14.6% yoy and amounted to PLN 64.1 million. In 2019 as a whole, the Press segment's total revenue decreased by 10.8% yoy and amounted to PLN 254.7 million. In both periods, the decrease in revenue was driven mainly by negative trends in the press advertising market and reduction of the scale of Agora's printing activities. On the other hand, the segment's revenue was positively affected by the increase in digital revenue generated by the daily, related both to a higher number of digital subscriptions and higher advertising revenue of the Wyborcza.pl websites. As at the end of 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza's digital revenue accounted for 24.0% of the daily's total revenue.
1.1. Copy sales
Both in the fourth quarter of 2019 and in the entire 2019, the segment's revenue from copy sales increased. They increased by 0.3% yoy to PLN 28.9 million in the fourth quarter of 2019, and by 2.7% to PLN 109.7 million in 2019 as a whole. That was primarily a result of higher revenue from content subscriptions of Wyborcza.pl. It is worth noting that the number of active paid digital subscriptions of Wyborcza.pl reached nearly 218 thousand at the end of December 2019, which means an increase by almost 28.0% yoy.
Both in the fourth quarter and in the entire 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza maintained its leading position in sales among the opinion-forming dailies. In the fourth quarter of 2019, the average paid distribution of Gazeta Wyborcza amounted to 94.6 thousand copies and decreased by 12.2% yoy. In the fourth quarter of 2019, revenue from sales of Gazeta Wyborcza's content picked up by 1.5% yoy.
In 2019, the average paid distribution of Gazeta Wyborcza amounted to 96.7 thousand copies and decreased by 9.0% yoy. In that period, revenue from sales of Gazeta Wyborcza increased by 6.5%. A steady increase in the number of digital subscriptions of Wyborcza.pl, which amounted to 218 thousand at the end of December 2019, had a positive effect on revenue from sales of the daily.
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 34

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
The aggregate data shows that in the fourth quarter of 2019 as many as 300 thousand people had access to paid content of Gazeta Wyborcza ­ traditional and digital editions in the form of subscriptions of Wyborcza.pl. In 2019, as many as 9 million people a month read the texts of Gazeta Wyborcza. These figures combine the data on readers of the paper edition, Internet subscription, digital application and electronic edition of Gazeta Wyborcza. They were compiled on the basis of data from the Polish Readership Survey and the Gemius PBI survey.
However, sales of periodicals and magazines decreased, mainly due to the reduced number of titles published. The decrease in revenue was mostly affected by the lack of revenue from sales of Dziecko, Ladny Dom and Cztery Kty. As a result, revenue from copy sales of Gazeta Wyborcza's periodicals and magazines decreased by 10.7% yoy to PLN 2.5 million in the fourth quarter of 2019, and by 20.0% yoy to PLN 11.2 million in 2019.
1.2. Advertising sales [3]
In the fourth quarter of 2019, advertising revenue in the Press segment declined by 19.6% yoy to PLN 22.6 million. In 2019 as a whole, they were lower by 16.6% yoy and stood at PLN 84.8 million. In both periods, this was mainly attributable to lower sales of advertising services in the paper edition of Gazeta Wyborcza and the absence of revenue from magazines that have been suspended or sold (Cztery Kty, Ladny Dom, Dziecko and Niezbdnik Ogrodnika).
In the fourth quarter of 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza's net advertising revenue from all of its advertising activity amounted to PLN 19.1 million (down by 14.7% yoy). In 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza's net advertising revenue from all of its advertising activity decreased by 11.6% yoy to PLN 71.5 million. The decreases were primarily caused by advertisers' cut-downs on printed press expenditure by 11.5%.
Apart from the trends in the printed press market, the dynamics of advertising sales of Gazeta Wyborcza's periodicals and magazines in 2019 was adversely affected by the decision to discontinue the publication or sales of selected titles. As a result, sales of advertisements in Gazeta Wyborcza's periodicals and magazines decreased by 36.4% yoy to PLN 13.1 million in 2019.
1.3. Printing services
Both in the fourth quarter of 2019 and in the entire 2019, the Print division's revenue from sales of printing services to external customers decreased yoy to PLN 10.5 million and PLN 47.2 million, respectively. The significant drop in revenue from printing services resulted primarily from the shutdown of two out of the Agora Group's three printing plants and from a lower volume of orders for printing services.
2. COST
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Press segment's operating costs excluding IFRS 16 were reduced by 30.1% yoy to PLN 57.5 million, and in the entire 2019 ­ by 18.5% yoy to PLN 260.1 million. The comparability of the segment's operating costs in 2019 with the corresponding period of 2018 was significantly affected by the recognition of impairment losses on receivables from RUCH S.A. in 2018, in the amount of PLN 20.3 million (PLN 16.3 million in the second quarter of 2018 and PLN 4.0 million in the fourth quarter of 2018), as well as recognition of impairment losses related to selected magazines in the fourth quarter of 2018, in the amount of PLN 2.3 million. Additionally, in 2018 the segment incurred restructuring costs of PLN 3.6 million. In 2019, the segment's results were affected by restructuring costs of printing operations in the amount of PLN 4.9 million.
A key factor contributing to the reduction in the segment's operating costs both in the fourth quarter and in the entire 2019 were lower yoy costs of materials, energy, goods and printing services which resulted from the reduction of printing services and lower printing volume of the titles published. In the fourth quarter of 2019, this category of costs decreased by 31.8% yoy to PLN 17.8 million, and in 2019 ­ by 17.8% yoy to PLN 82.0 million.
In addition, in the fourth quarter of 2019 and in 2019 as a whole, staff costs were reduced by 16.7% yoy and 10.4% yoy, respectively. This was mainly attributable to a lower number of full-time employees which resulted from the reduction in headcount as part of the collective redundancies process carried out in the first quarter of 2019 with respect to the restructuring of printing activities.
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 35

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
Both in the fourth quarter and in the entire 2019, depreciation costs decreased significantly ­ by 68.6% yoy and 23.5% yoy, respectively. This was related to the phasing out of two out of three of the Agora Group's printing plants at the end of the second quarter of 2019.
3. NEW INITIATIVES
In the fourth quarter of 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza's team announced another success in the digital area: at the end of September, the number of active subscriptions of Wyborcza.pl exceeded 200 thousand and at the end of December 2019 ­ nearly 218 thousand. Only the top prestigious press titles from around the world can boast such a result. The significant increase in the number of Wyborcza.pl subscriptions recorded in 2019 was mainly due to changes in the offering introduced since February 2019, such as family access, possibility to read printed edition of Gazeta Wyborcza online or to share unlocked articles with friends and family, extension of the portfolio dedicated to recipients from companies and institutions, as well as measures aimed at increasing readers' engagement. Throughout 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza also prepared attractive offers for Internet users. At the beginning of October 2019, Klub Przyjaciól Wyborczej (Wyborcza Friends' Club) was established. Digital subscribers of the daily who decide to purchase a special subscription and support Gazeta Wyborcza may participate free of charge in meetings, discussions and interactions with the editorial team held especially for them. They will also receive invitations to events held across Poland, including regular meetings such as Centrum Premier Czerska 8/10, Kobiety wiedz, co robi and Wyborcza na ywo, as well as a selection of attractive discounts from partners such as the Agora Publishing House.
The Wyborcza.pl team has also been developing its newsletter portfolio - in November 2019, a new edition of the local Wyborcza.pl newsletter was launched under the Dzie dobry (Good morning) brand. Every day before 8.00 a.m., its subscribers receive information about 1 out of 20 Polish cities, a commentary by a journalist or editor of the local editorial office of Gazeta Wyborcza, a weather forecast and air quality data, as well as links to the most interesting local publications on Wyborcza.pl. Another newsletter ­ but this time focused on environmental issues ­ served as the basis for a unique, pro-environmental campaign of Wyborcza.pl and Wysokieobcasy.pl prepared in cooperation with a telecommunications network, under the slogan Bez ladu - Od Ciebie zaley, jaki zostawisz po sobie lad (Without a trace ­ what will you leave behind depends on you). In general, at the end of 2019 the daily's team offered several dozen newsletters to Internet users, covering attractive topics, such as books, TV series or a recap of most important events of the day. All of them allow the editorial team to engage readers even more and tell them stories about the world in a more personal, direct and regular manner. Another unique project is Gazeta Wyborcza's podcast called 8:10, available since December 2019. In subsequent episodes of the series, published free of charge on, among others, Wyborcza.pl and podcast platforms from Monday to Friday from 8.10 a.m., journalists of Gazeta Wyborcza and Wyborcza.pl comment on the most important events in Poland and worldwide, recommend cultural events and talk about their texts. The new podcast of Gazeta Wyborcza is a unique opportunity to not only read but also hear about the events, developments and people described in the newspaper.
The editorial team also focuses on the development of the traditional edition of Gazeta Wyborcza by, among others, offering its readers attractive additions and special issues. In October 2019, one of the year's largest editions of the daily was published, featuring a special magazine entitled The Big Ideas. Wladza (Authority), prepared in collaboration with a team from the New York Times. The answer to the question "What is authority?" was sought by scientists, writers and journalists invited by the NYT editorial team, including Yuval Noah Harari, Susan Fowler and Ivan Krastev. At the end of December 2019, the editors prepared the third special edition of Wysokie Obcasy, dedicated exclusively to women who were the heroines of 2019. The group of 50 bold women described included Olga Tokarczuk, Krystyna Janda, Agnieszka Holland, Martyna Wojciechowska and others. On the last day of 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza was sold together with the Turning Points magazine, also prepared in cooperation with the NYT's editorial team. The readers had the opportunity to read the reflections of eminent people from politics, business, science and culture, regarding the events that may move the world in the coming year. Apart from that, in the fourth quarter the Gazeta Wyborcza's team prepared special editions of Magazyn witeczny (The Holiday Magazine) ­ Na Pierwszy Snieg (For the first snowfall) and Na Wspólne wita (Christmas Together), as well as ­ for 1 November ­ Którzy odeszli (The Ones who passed away) magazine, commemorating over 130 people who died in 2019. Two magazines were also sold independently: a special issue of Wysokie Obcasy ­ Psychologia dla rodziców. Pokolenie smartfona (Wysokie Obcasy ­Psychology for parents. The smartphone generation), and Na narty (Let's go skiing), addressed to skiers with different skill levels. Since November 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza's issues are available at a changed price ­ the issues from Wednesday to Saturday are 50 grosz

more expensive. The change was mainly related to the overall increase in costs, including costs of energy and services. Also since November 2019, business customers of Gazeta Wyborcza and Wyborcza.pl may benefit from a new solution combining the sale of digital subscriptions for a specific group of recipients with additional advertising benefits. The sponsorship of digital subscriptions was added to Gazeta Wyborcza's Internet offering for companies and institutions. This offering also includes display campaigns, special projects, content marketing solutions and newsletter partnerships. An additional option for companies and institutions cooperating with Gazeta Wyborcza and Wyborcza.pl is the patronage ­ a grant to the Gazeta Wyborcza Foundation that will be used by the organization to purchase Wyborcza.pl subscriptions for students, university employees, libraries and other entities. To each subscription funded by the sponsor, the Gazeta Wyborcza Foundation adds another one on its own. In May 2019 the daily celebrated its 30th anniversary. On 4 June 2019, the new design of the Gazeta Wyborcza mockup was presented. It was prepared by Jacek Utko, a recognised creator of graphic designs of newspapers from all over the world. The daily has gained a modern and consistent layout, presented in a more structured way, making it clearer and more readable. Throughout 2019, Gazeta Wyborcza willingly engaged in international initiatives. In March, it joined this year's edition of Google News Initiative Fellowship, offering a journalistic internship. It also launched the Europe Talks platform, connecting people with different political views from all over Europe as part of cooperation between over 15 media before the European Parliament elections. The editors of Gazeta Wyborcza also united forces with the teams of Le Soir, Le Figaro and El Pais, which belong to the prestigious European LENA association (Leading European Newspaper Alliance), creating a new media project called Sonar Europe. As a result, attractive multimedia data-based materials have been created, concerning a variety of subjects and presenting diverse points of view from different countries of the European Union. Like every year, the Press segment's team was also involved in the organisation of Agora's music and cultural festivals. In June 2019, the local summer Co Jest Grane Festival took place for the fourth time, and a concert was organised opening a cycle of events entitled Women's Voices. This year, it was organised under the slogan `Women save the planet'. During the summer holidays, fans of music and literature had the opportunity to take part in: the second edition of Bialystok New Pop Festival, the second edition of the #bdzieczytane Elk Festiwal ­ an event that promotes literature, reading and music, as well as the sixth edition of the Olsztyn Green Festival which featured such stars of the Polish popular music as Nosowska, Andrzej Piaseczny, VOO VOO, Pawel Domagala, Mrozu, Ørganek, Krzysztof Zalewski and The Dumplings. All festivals were accompanied by a number of additional events that promoted e.g. ecology and a healthy lifestyle, as well as events prepared for the youngest participants. An important change related to the printing business of the Agora Group was made in 2019. In the face of unfavorable market trends and in response to a reduction in the volume of orders from external customers, especially for coldset printing, the Group has decided to reduce this business ­ by shutting down two out of three printing plants and reducing employment by means of collective redundancies. Since the third quarter of 2019, the optimized printing business of the Agora Group, including one printing plant located in Warsaw, has been part of the Press segment.

In the fourth quarter of 2019, an increase in the Outdoor segment's revenue by 8.2% yoy to PLN 55.6 million translated into a significant improvement yoy in the segment's performance. The segment's EBIT excluding IFRS 16 increased by 10.2% yoy to PLN 11.9 million. The segment also reported an improvement in EBITDA excluding IFRS 16 ­ to 17.0 million, and in EBITDA margin excluding IFRS 16 ­ to 30.6%. Over 2019, owing to a 7.2% yoy increase in revenue, the Outdoor segment's EBIT excluding IFRS 16 improved by 10.7% yoy to PLN 29.9 million. In that period, the segment's result at the EBITDA level excluding IFRS 16 increased by 6.0% yoy to PLN 49.5 million, whereas the EBITDA margin excluding IFRS 16 stood at 26.9%.

[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 38

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
It is worth noting that the purchase of a majority stake in Piano Group Sp. z o.o. in July 2019 contributed positively to the segment's performance in both analyzed periods.
The Outdoor segment is one of the Group's businesses for which the adoption of IFRS 16 means a change in the presentation of its results. Data for previous periods are not comparable. After the entry into force of IFRS 16, the specified long-term lease agreements have ceased to be included in the cost of system maintenance. At the same time, the AMS balance sheet recognised assets (rights to use space) equal to the discounted amount of future payments under lease agreements. Depreciation of this right increases depreciation costs recognised in the segment's income statement. At the same time, in connection with the obligation to pay the discounted lease charges, part of the costs is recognised as interest on lease liabilities, and it is charged to the financial costs. Such recognition increases depreciation and the segment's result at the EBITDA level.
As a result, in the fourth quarter of 2019, the segment's EBIT, according to IFRS 16, amounted to PLN 12.3 million, and the segment's EBITDA ­ PLN 21.5 million. In 2019 as a whole, the Outdoor segment's EBIT, in accordance with IFRS 16, amounted to PLN 30.8 million, and the segment's EBITDA ­ to PLN 62.3 million.
1. REVENUE [8]
In the fourth quarter of 2019, outdoor advertising spending, as estimated by IGRZ (the Outdoor Advertising Chamber), increased by more than 8.8% yoy. In 2019 as a whole, outdoor advertising spending increased by nearly 5.1% yoy [8].
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Outdoor segment's advertising sales increased by 5.3% yoy and amounted to PLN 53.6 million. This increase was driven chiefly by increased advertisers' spending on campaigns carried out on panels in the Premium Citylight and Digital segment, including on the MoveTV platform.
In 2019 as a whole, the increase in revenues from AMS advertising sales was higher than the expenditure increase in the outdoor advertising market reported by IGRZ, amounting to 6.1%. The growth of AMS revenue was boosted by advertisers' spending on campaigns carried out on Premium Citylight and Digital panels, including on the MoveTV platform.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the estimated share of AMS in outdoor advertising spending, monitored by IGRZ, amounted to nearly 34.0%, and throughout 2019 ­ to over 34.0% [8].
2. COST
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the segment's operating costs excluding IFRS 16 increased by 7.6% yoy to PLN 43.7 million, mainly due to higher staff costs, promotion and marketing costs, and system maintenance costs. These expenditures were driven by costs related to operations of Piano Group Sp. z o. o., the owner of the MoveTV platform.
The 41.7% yoy increase in staff costs in the period in question is primarily attributable to provisions recognised for the Group's incentive schemes. These costs were also significantly driven by the costs of professional training provided for the sales department.
The increase in promotion and marketing costs by 52.9% yoy in the fourth quarter of 2019 was triggered primarily by expenditure on advertising campaigns and other promotion costs settled in the form of barter.
The 4.9% yoy increase in system maintenance costs (excluding IFRS 16) is mainly attributable to higher expenditure on lease of advertising space on public transport shelters in Poznan and increased costs of lighting of advertising panels.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the costs of executed campaigns declined by 7.1% yoy to PLN 6.5 million, reflecting lower costs of poster replacement, a smaller number of non-standard projects and a smaller number of advertising campaigns executed on public transport vehicles.
In 2019 as a whole, the segment's operating costs excluding IFRS 16 increased by 6.6% yoy to PLN 154.4 million. This increase is mainly attributable to higher staff costs, system maintenance costs, as well as promotion and marketing costs. These expenditures were driven by costs related to operations of Piano Group Sp. z o. o., the owner of the MoveTV platform.
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 39

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
System maintenance costs excluding IFRS 16 increased by 3.0% yoy due to an increase in expenditure on the lease of advertising space on public transport shelters in Poznan, lighting and ongoing maintenance and repair of advertising panels.
The increase in staff costs by 13.4% to PLN 26.3 million over the entire 2019 is mainly due to the recognition of provisions for the Group's incentive schemes and an increase in variable remuneration components as a result of better performance in terms of sales targets. These costs were also driven by the costs of professional training provided for the sales department.
The increase in promotion and marketing costs to PLN 6.9 million in 2019 resulted mainly from expenditure on advertising campaigns, other promotion costs settled in the form of barter and higher total costs of nonprofit/commercial campaigns, where the non-profit part is settled in the form of barter and charged to promotion and marketing cost.
The segment's operating costs presented in accordance with IFRS 16 amounted to PLN 43.3 million in the fourth quarter of 2019 and PLN 153.5 million in the entire 2019. The implementation of the above standard exerted the greatest impact on the cost of system maintenance and depreciation, which amounted to PLN 10.5 million and PLN 9.1 million in the fourth quarter of 2019, and PLN 44.9 million and PLN 31.4 million in the entire 2019, respectively.
3. NEW INITIATIVES
AMS consistently conducts activities aimed at implementing the idea of a smart city - creating an intelligent city through ecological, innovative and functional solutions. The company's innovative green public transport shelters and environmentally friendly solar pole were presented at the Open Eyes Economy Summit in Krakow.
AMS continued to implement further campaigns, exploiting primarily the potential of the premium panels. They included, for example, a multi-format Christmas campaign of a jewellery brand involving, among others, attractive Dynamic Backlight and Citylight panels in an advertising pole, as well as activities for a food brand with a special arrangement of panels at public transport stops in Krakow. Additionally, as part of the next edition of the Warsaw fair Targi Rzeczy Ladnych, held in November 2019, two AMS exhibitions were showcased - posters from the last edition of the AMS Poster Gallery competition presented, among others, on panels coupled with city furniture. The presentations were accompanied by Digital Citylight - a digital panel that displayed a film about the AMS Poster Gallery and posters with the slogan: "Zwierz te czlowiek" (Animal is also a human).
The exceptional ability of the DOOH solutions to react immediately to current events was proved by the news of the Nobel Prize for Literature awarded to Olga Tokarczuk - on the same day, AMS congratulated the writer on this award and informed the residents of Wroclaw about it on Cityscreen panels.
Since December 2019, AMS has been using the Cityinfo panels to display economic flashcards ­ TEPiszki. It is an educational cycle prepared in cooperation with the Association of Polish Economists (TEP), intended to support the broadening of social awareness and to promote economic knowledge. Cityinfo is a constantly updated city information and advertising service, prepared by a professional team. The information is presented in categories such as travel, fashion and beauty, fitness, health, interiors, what-where-when, and - since December - also in the economics section.
In April 2019, AMS introduced a new price list with a new trade policy, based on the principle of transparency and linking the price of the medium to the size of the audience it generates. This is the result of the implementation of the results of the Outdoor Track advertising panels study carried out by Instytut Bada Outdooru IBO Sp. z o.o.. In 2019, AMS customers had the opportunity to choose to use AMS services under the existing or new conditions, and the company's representatives provided training to customers on the use of new tools in the outdoor planning process.
A significant change experienced by the company in 2019 was the acquisition carried out in July ­ AMS became the majority shareholder of the Piano Group which operates in digital out of home (DOOH) segment, acting as an operator of the MoveTV platform with screens in the largest fitness clubs in Poland and original premium content adapted to watch during training. With this transaction, AMS ­ the leading player in the Polish outdoor advertising market, expanded its portfolio with a new type of media and strengthened its position in the DOOH segment in line with the development strategy of the Agora Group. The MoveTV platform, owned by the Piano Group, is currently using 970 screens located in more than 240 largest fitness clubs in 30 cities in Poland, as well as in the Czech Republic and Bulgaria. MoveTV joined the channels in the digital portfolio of AMS media which also includes
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 40

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only advertising on ATM screens, in public transport and shopping malls, as well as Digital Citylight, Digital Cityscreen and Dynamic Backlight panels. AMS has also been systematically increasing the number of Premium Citylight panels in its portfolio. In March, it signed a long-term contract with MPK Lód to modernize over 250 public transport shelters. After renovation, each of them will be fitted with at least three Premium Citylight advertising panels. The new design of the bus and tram shelters will be determined not only by advertisement panels, but also modernised benches, timetables and energy-saving LED bars that illuminate the interior and exterior of the stop platform. In June 2019, AMS concluded a contract with Midzynarodowe Targi Poznaskie (Poznan International Fair) on the basis of which it became an operator of advertisements on public transport shelters in Poznan as of 1 July 2019, for the next 10 years. Under the contract, citylight panels in Poznan will be modernized and offered in premium standard within three years. Cooperation between AMS and MTP refers to 1,153 advertising spaces and will be expanded to include more shelters. AMS' performance is appreciated and rewarded by the market. For the tenth time in a row, the sales team was awarded the honourable title of the OOH Advertising Office of the Year, and in the Pearls of the Polish Economy ranking, AMS went up to the 11th place.

In the fourth quarter of 2019, the result of the Internet segment at the EBIT level excluding IFRS 16 increased to PLN 4.4 million ­ mainly due to an increase in the operating result of Gazeta.pl and Yieldbird. In 2019 as a whole, the segment's EBIT excluding IFRS 16 declined yoy to PLN 14.3 million. This was caused primarily by increased costs of external services ­ particularly sales brokerage costs of Yieldbird. In the fourth quarter of 2019, the segment's EBITDA excluding IFRS 16 stood at PLN 13.9 million [1] (up by 14.9% yoy). That was the effect of better results of Gazeta.pl and Yieldbird. Throughout 2019, EBITDA excluding IFRS 16 increased by 1.8% yoy and reached PLN 28.9 million [1].
The implementation of IFRS 16 had no significant effect on the recognition of the operating costs in the Internet segment or the segment's operating profits.
1. REVENUE
In the fourth quarter of 2019, total revenue of the Internet segment increased by 45.6% yoy to PLN 74.7 million. Significantly higher advertising sales generated by Yieldbird (including on Gazeta.pl's space) and full consolidation

[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 42

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
of HRlink Sp. z o.o. (formerly: Online Technologies HR Sp. z o.o.) as of September 2019 were the main factors behind the increase in the segment's revenue. In 2019, the Internet segment's total revenue increased by 17.5% yoy, mainly owing to higher online advertising sales reported by Yieldbird. The segment's revenue in both periods in question was negatively affected by the discontinuation of Agora Performance operations in November 2018 and lower revenue generated by GoldenLine.
2. COST
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Internet segment's operating costs excluding IFRS 16 went up by 45.2%, yoy and in 2019 as a whole ­ they increased by 20.0% yoy to PLN 194.7 million. The increase in operating costs was largely driven by higher spending on external services, associated mainly with the lease of advertising space ­ primarily in Yieldbird, and depreciation costs.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, costs of external services excluding IFRS 16 increased to PLN 42.6 million, and in 2019 ­ to PLN 113.1 million. This increase was mostly driven by higher lease costs of advertising space for Yieldbird. However, the increase in this cost category was offset by higher revenue from advertising sales.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, staff costs decreased by 6.2% yoy to PLN 12.2 million, and in the period from January to December ­ they declined by 7.9% yoy to PLN 50.0 million. That was mainly the effect of the reduced number of full-time employees, mainly in Gazeta.pl and GoldenLine.
Depreciation costs excluding IFRS 16 were higher both in the fourth quarter and throughout 2019 ­ by 23.5% yoy and 35.8% yoy, respectively. The increase in these costs was mostly driven by investments made to modernize the technical infrastructure, which allowed for the development of advertising products and improvement of Gazeta.pl's visibility in search results of the most popular search engines. In addition, investment projects implemented in Yieldbird, GoldenLine and Domiporta contributed to the increase in depreciation costs.
In the third quarter of 2019, promotion and marketing costs decreased by 8.3% yoy. In 2019, the decrease in expenditure on marketing and promotion was 17.8% yoy and was associated with lower expenditure on promotion in GoldenLine and Domiporta, as well as lower barter costs in Gazeta.pl.
3. IMPORTANT INFORMATION ON INTERNET ACTIVITIES
In December 2019, the overall reach of the Gazeta.pl group websites among Polish Internet users stood at 59.0%, and the number of users reached 16.3 million, which made the Gazeta.pl group the ninth market player according to a survey by Gemius PBI. The total number of page views of the Gazeta.pl group websites reached 526 million, with the average viewing time of 42 minutes per user [6].
In December 2019, 12.7 million Internet users viewed the websites of Gazeta.pl group on mobile devices. The number of mobile page views amounted to 382 million, and the share of mobile page views on the websites of Gazeta.pl group stood at 73.0% and was the highest among Polish horizontal web portals [6].
The websites of Gazeta.pl group are ranked among the top thematic market players. In accordance with the data from Gemius PBI for December 2019, Gazeta.pl group is the runner-up in the "Gossip, celebrity life" (Plotek.pl), "Local and regional news" (e.g. local websites of Wyborcza.pl and Metrowarszawa.pl) and "Children and family" (eDziecko.pl) categories. The websites of Gazeta.pl group are also highly ranked in the following categories: "Information & journalism ­ general" (third place, e.g. Wyborcza.pl and Wiadomosci.Gazeta.pl), "Sports" (also third place, e.g. Sport.pl), "Websites for women" (fourth place, Kobieta.Gazeta.pl and Wysokieobcasy.pl), "Fashion and beauty" (fourth place, Avanti24.pl), "Automotive"(sixth place, Moto.pl), "Diets, slimming, fitness" (sixth place, e.g. Myfitness.Gazeta.pl).
4. NEW INITIATIVES
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the editorial team of the Gazeta.pl portal and websites prepared a number novelties for their users. In October, the video format entitled Marketing Master Class ­ conversations with the masters of Polish marketing ­ had its premiere at Next.Gazeta.pl. These are short interviews with experienced managers about the condition of Polish marketing sector, carried out by Gazeta.pl in collaboration with CPC, a consulting
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 43

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
company. Earlier in 2019, Gazeta.pl's websites and homepage launched a number of new formats, including: live video business and lifestyle format Studio Biznes and two video formats created by Sport.pl ­ Football Section and F1 Sport. Gazeta.pl has also got involved in social and environmental protection initiatives ­ these topics are important for the editorial team who regularly publishes the cycle "Fridays for the climate" and expands the "Environment" section on the homepage. In October 2019, the portal supported the Greenpeace Poland Foundation's campaign Adopt a bee, once again encouraging everyone to virtually adopt bees, read articles on their lives and solve a special quiz about these insects. As every year, a bee appeared next to Gazeta.pl logo for one day. In December, the Gazeta.pl editorial team provided its readers with an overview of Greenpeace's activities ­ the homepage featured a live broadcast prepared by journalists together with members of the organization, as well as photos and recordings of its most interesting campaigns. In 2019, Gazeta.pl also introduced a number of new solutions for its customers ­ in June, for example, the portal's team connected the ABT Shield tool, created by Edge NPD, to all their websites, in order to enhance the protection of users and advertisers. This is an innovative solution that uses artificial intelligence to limit the distribution of misleading information as well as the negative impact of bots and trolls on the experience of readers and the effectiveness of advertising campaigns. The last months of 2019 were also productive for Internet companies from the Agora Group. In October 2019, Yieldbird joined IAB Europe, the leading organisation for the European digital advertising ecosystem. The company from the Agora Group, specializing in optimizing publishers' advertising resources, became the second Polish member of this association. In November, the company's team organized the second edition of YieldFest ­ a meeting for publishers interested in programming advertising in Poland, this time under the slogan Challenges and trends for 2020. Earlier in 2019, Yieldbird continued to develop international operations, as it attracted new customers in the United States, Denmark, Ireland and Serbia, and established partnerships in Brasil and Nordic countries. 2019 also saw important changes in Agora's Internet company portfolio. In June, in line with the investment agreement concluded in September 2018, Agora acquired further shares in ROI Hunter during the second round of financing, and currently holds 24% of the company's shares. In 2019 ROI Hunter has been intensively expanding its offering for marketers. In September 2019, Agora became the majority shareholder of HRlink Sp. z o.o., a company that develops an original HRlink.pl application that is used to optimize and modernize e-recruitment processes. With this transaction, Agora consolidated its position in the market of recruitment and B2B services. Agora has been the shareholder of HRlink Sp. z o.o. since 2012.

IV.E. RADIO

The Radio segment includes the pro-forma consolidated financials of Agora's Radio Department, all local radio stations and a super-regional radio TOK FM, which are parts of the Agora Group. These include: 24 Golden Hits (Zlote Przeboje) local radio stations (in August 2018, Radio Zlote Przeboje started broadcasting in Wetlina, Bieszczady), 4 local radio stations under the brand Rock Radio, 8 local stations broadcasting under the brand Radio Pogoda (since March 2018 Radio Pogoda broadcasts in Gdansk) and a super-regional news radio TOK FM broadcasting in 23 metropolitan areas.

(1) advertising revenues include revenues from brokerage services of proprietary and third-party air time;
(2) the amounts do not include revenues and total cost of cross-promotion of Agora's different media (only the direct variable cost of campaigns carried out on advertising panels) if such a promotion was executed without prior reservation.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the operating profits of the Radio segment excluding IFRS 16, both at the EBIT and EBITDA levels, were lower yoy and amounted to PLN 7.1 million and PLN 8.2 million, respectively. In 2019 as a whole, the segment's EBIT excluding IFRS 16 declined yoy to PLN 14.2 million. In the same period, the segment's EBITDA excluding IFRS 16 also decreased yoy to PLN 18.5 million.
The results of the segment were mainly affected by lower sales of advertising services in the segment's own stations, higher costs of promotion and marketing (throughout 2019) and higher staff costs.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the segment's operating profit at the EBIT level, according to IFRS 16, was PLN 7.1 million, and the segment's EBITDA ­ PLN 8.8 million. In 2019 as a whole, the segment's EBIT, reported according to IFRS 16, amounted to PLN 14.4 million, and EBITDA stood at PLN 21.4 million.

1. REVENUE [3]
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the Radio segment's revenue decreased by 1.6% yoy and stood at PLN 37.5 million. This was chiefly due to lower revenue from brokerage of third-party airtime.
In the fourth quarter of 2019, radio advertising spending in the market increased by 0.2% yoy. Over the same period, sales of radio advertising in the Radio segment dropped by 3.7%.

[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 45

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
In 2019 as a whole, the Radio segment's revenue decreased by 2.5% yoy to PLN 113.1 million. The decrease in the segment's revenue is attributable primarily to lower revenue from brokerage of third-party airtime, as well as lower air time sales in the radio stations of the Agora Radio Group. However, in the period in questions, revenue from brokerage services provided for Helios network cinemas increased. In 2019, radio advertising spending in the market decreased by 0.3% yoy, whereas sales of radio advertising in the Radio segment declined by 5.6% yoy.
2. COST
In the fourth quarter of 2019, the operating costs of the Radio segment excluding IFRS 16 decreased by 1.3% yoy to PLN 30.4 million.
In the period in question, the costs of external services excluding IFRS 16 decreased by 3.3% yoy to PLN 11.8 million. This cost item was mostly affected by lower expenditure related to brokerage of third-party airtime. At the same time, the costs related to the sales brokerage services for the Helios cinema network were higher yoy. Apart from the costs of sales brokerage for Helios cinemas and the costs related to the advertising sales brokerage for third-party radio stations, the external services cost item (excluding IFRS 16) also includes rental and lease fees, production services as well as operator fees.
In 2019 as a whole, the segment's operating costs excluding IFRS 16 increased by 0.1% yoy to PLN 98.9 million.
Promotion and marketing costs increased by 16.5% yoy to PLN 14.1 million. Their increase was related to the promotion of Radio Zlote Przeboje, Rock Radio and Radio Pogoda, as well as sales promotion.
There was also an increase yoy in staff costs, which were reported at PLN 34.6 million. This was mainly due to an increase in the cost of full-time salaries and costs of courses, training and conferences.
In the period from January to December 2019, the costs of external services excluding IFRS 16 decreased by 8.7% yoy to PLN 39.0 million. This cost item was primarily affected by lower spending on air time purchases in thirdparty radio stations in connection with the brokerage service provided and lower marketing research costs. At the same time, the costs related to the sales brokerage services for the Helios cinema network were higher yoy.
The operating costs of the Radio segment presented according to IFRS 16 stood at PLN 30.4 million in the fourth quarter of 2019 and at PLN 98.7 million in the entire 2019.

4. NEW INITIATIVES
Radio TOK FM closed 2019 with another success of its paid podcast offer ­ at the end of December, the number of TOK FM Premium subscriptions purchased exceeded 20 thousand. This is a 20% increase since March 2019. For 6 years, Agora's Radio Group has been continuously developing the TOK FM digital offering, adding new content and functionalities to make it as convenient to use as possible. To this end, in 2019, among other things, it expanded the portfolio of its own podcasts, including those created exclusively online, as well as partner broadcasts presented on the tokfm.pl platform and in the TOK FM application. This way, since mid-October 2019, a 6-part reporter's series entitled "ledztwo Pisma" (Pismo's Investigation) was released, which enjoyed great popularity, and since December ­ also a podcast from Gazeta Wyborcza entitled "8:10". In addition, in 2019 the TOK FM team implemented technological innovations ­ a special feature in the Google Assistant allowing for voice control of TOK FM Radio in the Polish language version, as well as the Search the Radio project that makes it possible to search through the fully transcribed content of radio shows. While striving for the development of its subscription offer, Radio TOK FM also promoted its mobile application. In August 2019, advertisments with the slogans Sluchaj, gdziekolwiek jestes (Listen, wherever you are) and Wszystko co wazne, gdziekolwiek jestes (Everything that

[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 46

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
matters, wherever you are) appeared on outdoor advertising panels in several Polish cities. In this way, the station encouraged its listeners to use the TOK FM application in order to listen to both the live radio and podcasts in any place and at any time. All this, combined with the popularity of podcasts and content subscriptions, allowed for another significant leap in the development of the TOK FM Premium offering ­ over the last 2 years, the subscriber base has increased by 100%. Additionally, in the fourth quarter of 2019, everyone who was interested in podcasts could learn interesting conclusions from the so far most extensive survey of Polish podcast listeners prepared for Tandem Media, an advertising broker from the Agora Radio Group. According to data presented in November, as many as 27% of Internet users in Poland listen to podcasts. Most of them listen to podcasts at least once a month, using headphones and a smartphone ­ at home or on the move, for entertainment and to learn more about the world. At the same time, podcast listeners, although most of them started to listen to them only a year ago, devote their full attention to podcasts and evaluate their credibility higher than that of traditional media, and are more receptive to the advertising forms associated with them. These conclusions support the expansion of TOK FM's digital offering in the form of podcasts and development of attractive advertising solutions for the partners of the Agora Radio Group. In addition, in October 2019 Radio TOK FM completed a major project related to the elections ­ this time to the Sejm and Senate. From September, as part of the Wybory w TOKu campaign, the station broadcasted special programmes and guides, and organized 17 debates under the slogan Uslysz swojego posla (Hear your deputy) with candidates for MPs ­ eight debates in Polish cities with the participation of the audience and nine debates in the radio studio. The campaign ended with Wieczór wyborczy (Election's evening), aired after the end of voting on Sunday, 13 October, and Poranek powyborczy (Post-election's morning) aired on Monday. Additionally, Gazeta.pl and Radio TOK FM invited Internet users to a special post-election online video show ­ for almost six hours, Internet users could watch live, on the station's website and on Agora's portal and in social media, hot political discussions as well as analyses and comments on the results of the election. Earlier in 2019, Radio TOK FM carried out a similar campaign under the slogan Nasza Europa (Our Europe). This campaign included six debates with candidates to the European Parliament in six Polish cities and discussions in the studio dedicated to other electoral regions. Each conversation was transmitted live on TOK FM Radio as well as on Tokfm.pl in a video format. Furthermore, in spring of 2019, Radio Zlote Przeboje, Rock Radio and Radio Pogoda launched their newest mobile applications in AppStore and Google Play. Not only do they offer the opportunity to listen to live broadcasts, with local station selection and viewing of the songs being played, but they also make it possible to receive messages about new radio's initiatives and competitions. 2019 was also very important for the Agora Group in the context of consolidating its position on the radio market and possible further portfolio expansion. In February 2019 Agora acquired a minority stake in Eurozet Sp. z o.o. (40%), the second largest radio broadcaster in Poland, securing the possibility of acquiring the entire stake if it proves to be profitable in the future. In the autumn, the company announced its intention to purchase the remaining shares in Eurozet Sp. z o.o. (60%) and subsequently applied to the President of the Office of Competition and Consumer Protection (UOKiK) for approval of the transaction. For Agora, this transaction would mean another step in implementing its strategy for the development of its current businesses and strengthening its position in the radio market.

NOTES
[1] The performance measure "EBIT" represents net operating profit/(loss) defined as net profit/(loss) in accordance with IFRS before finance income and costs, share of results of equity accounted investees and income taxes.
The performance measure "EBITDA" is defined as EBIT increased by depreciation and amortization and impairment losses of property, plant and equipment and intangible assets.
In the Management Board opinion, EBITDA constitutes a useful supplementary financial indicator in assessing the performance of the Group and its operating segments. It should be taken into account, that EBIT and EBITDA are not measures determined by IFRS and have not a uniform standard of calculation. Accordingly, their calculation and presentation by the Group may differ from that applied by other companies.
EBIT and EBITDA of Press, Internet, Movies and Books, as well as Print segments are calculated on the basis of cost directly attributable to the appropriate operating segment of the Agora Group and excludes allocations of all Company's overheads (such as: cost of Agora's Management Board and a majority of cost of the Company`s supporting divisions), which are included in reconciling positions.
Moreover, EBIT of particular operating segments does not include depreciation and amortisation recognised on consolidation as described in note 22 to the consolidated financial statements.
[2] the data on ticket sales in the cinemas comprising Helios group come from the accounting data of Helios reported in accordance with full calendar periods.
[3] The data refer to advertising expenditures in six media (press, radio, TV, outdoor, Internet, cinema). In this MD&A Agora has corrected the numbers for dailies (in the third quarter of 2019) in TV ( in the fourth quarter of 2018 and in the second quarter of 2019), in internet (in in the first, second and third quarter of 2019 and fourth quarter of 2018).
Unless explicitly stated otherwise, press and radio advertising market data referred to herein are based on Agora's estimates adjusted for average discount rate and are stated in current prices. Given the discount pressure as well as advertising time and space sell-offs, these figures may not be fully reliable and will be adjusted in the consecutive reporting periods. In case of press, the data include only display advertising, excluding classifieds, inserts and obituaries. The estimates are based on rate card data obtained from the following sources: Kantar Media monitoring, Agora S.A. monitoring.
Presented TV, Internet and cinema figures are based on initial Starcom media house estimates; TV estimates include regular ad broadcast and sponsoring with product placement, exclude teleshopping and other advertising forms.
Internet ad spend estimates include display, search engines (Search Engine Marketing), e-mail marketing and video advertising.
Outdoor advertising figures are based on Izba Gospodarcza Reklamy Zewnetrznej and media house Starcomestimates [8].
The Company would like to stress that one should bear in mind that these advertising market estimations may represent some margin of error due to significant discount pressure on the market and lack of reliable data on the average market discount rates. Once the Company has a more reliable market data in consecutive quarters, it may correct the ad spending estimations in particular media.
[4] The data on the number of copies sold (total paid circulation) of daily newspapers is derived from the National Circulation Audit Office (ZKDP). The term "copy sales" used in this MD&A is consistent with the sales declarations of publishers to the National Circulation Audit Office.

2. CHANGES IN CAPITAL AFFILIATIONS AND ORGANISATION OF THE CAPITAL GROUP
Agora Finanse Sp. z o.o.

On June 6, 2019, the Extraordinary Shareholders Meeting of Agora Finanse Sp. z o.o. ("Agora Finanse") adopted a resolution on increasing the share capital of Agora Finanse from PLN 5 thousand to PLN 205 thousand by creating 4,000 new shares to be taken up by Agora S.A. On July 4, 2019, the District Court for Warsaw in Warsaw registered the above change. Currently, Agora S.A. holds 4,100 shares in Agora Finanse representing 100% of its share capital and giving rights to 4,100 votes representing 100% of the voting rights at the company's shareholders' meeting.

On December 23, 2019, the Extraordinary Shareholders Meeting of Agora Finanse Sp. z o.o. has decided to: (i) release the collateral established by Agora Finanse, as indicated in current report No. 13/2018 of May 18, 2018, (ii) agreeing to the redemption by Agora Finance Management Board of money market fund units.

Agora ­ Poligrafia Sp. z o.o.

On March 5, 2019, the Extraordinary Shareholders Meeting of Agora - Poligrafia Sp. z o.o. adopted a resolution on phasing out the business activities of Agora - Poligrafia Sp. z o.o. in the area of printing services. At the same time, the Extraordinary Shareholders Meeting of Agora - Poligrafia Sp. z o.o. stated that the said resolution did not represent a resolution on the dissolution of a company referred to in Article 270 point 2) of the Commercial Companies Code.

Doradztwo Mediowe Sp. z o.o.

On December 18, 2019, the Extraordinary Shareholders Meeting of Doradztwo Mediowe Sp. z o.o. adopted a resolution on consent to the payment of an advance dividend for 2019 to the sole shareholder.

Eurozet Sp. z o.o.

In the current report of January 25, 2019, the Management Board of Agora S.A. informed that the Company started negotiations regarding the potential acquisition of shares in Eurozet sp. o.o. with its registered office in Warsaw (`Eurozet') from their current owner.

The company started negotiations with the seller together with SFS Ventures s.r.o. with its registered office in Prague (Czech Republic) (`SFS Ventures') concerning the purchase of all the shares in the share capital of Eurozet as follows:

1.

SFS Ventures would acquire 60% of shares in Eurozet;

2.

Agora would acquire 40% of shares in Eurozet.

SFS Ventures is a company incorporated under Czech law. The majority stake is owned by a subsidiary, Sourcefabric z.ú., with its registered office in Prague (the Czech Republic), offering open source software solutions for the media and the minority stake is owned by Salvatorska Ventures LCC, a US registered subsidiary of Media Development Investment Fund.

At the same time, in connection with the commencement of the said negotiations, the Company also started negotiations with SFS Ventures to establish detailed principles of the potential investment in Eurozet by SFS

[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 53

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only

Ventures as a majority shareholder and the Company as a minority shareholder, as well as of the future cooperation of the two as shareholders of Eurozet.

The Company and SFS Ventures are conducting negotiations of the acquisition of shares in Eurozet on a nonexclusive basis. The potential transaction is in line with the long-term strategy of the Agora Group, in particular with the plan to strengthen the position of the Agora Group on selected markets on which it already operates.

In the current report of February 20, 2019, the Management Board of Agora S.A. informed on closing negotiations on: (i) acquisition of a legal title to shares in Eurozet Sp. z o.o. with its registered office in Warsaw (`Eurozet') and (ii) determination of detailed rules for an investment in Eurozet by SFS Ventures s.r.o. with its registered office in Prague (the Czech Republic) (`SFS Ventures') as a majority shareholder and the Company as a minority shareholder and the cooperation of both entities as shareholders of Eurozet.

As a result of the negotiations on February 20, 2019, the following were concluded:

1. a preliminary agreement on the sale of shares in the share capital of Eurozet (`Preliminary Agreement') between Czech Radio Centers., with its registered office in Prague (the Czech Republic), as a seller (`Seller'), Czech Media Invest a.s., with its registered office in Prague (the Czech Republic), as a guarantor of the Seller's obligations and:

a.

SFS Ventures, as a buyer of 60% of the shares in Eurozet, and

b.

the Company, as a buyer of 40% of the shares in Eurozet;

2. a final agreement for the sale of the above-mentioned shares in Eurozet, by and between the Company, SFS Ventures and the Seller (`Final Agreement'), concluded as part fulfilling the Preliminary Agreement, and

3. a shareholders' agreement between the Company and SFS Ventures regulating the detailed rules for investment in Eurozet by SFS Ventures, as a majority shareholder, and the Company as a minority shareholder and the cooperation of both entities as shareholders in Eurozet (`Shareholders' Agreement').

Under the Final Agreement, the Company acquired 400 shares in the share capital of Eurozet with a nominal value of PLN 50 each, representing 40% of the share capital of Eurozet and entitling the holder to exercise 40% of the total voting rights at the shareholders' meeting of Eurozet in exchange for an initial consideration of PLN 130,754,689. The Preliminary Agreement provides for an adjustment of the initial consideration based on the Eurozet Group's (`Group') audited financial statements for 2018 and the final values of certain economic and financial parameters of the Group, as set forth in the Preliminary Agreement.
As above, Agora, based on the audited financial statements for 2018, verified the purchase price and presented the final purchase price. The company does not anticipate a material adjustment to the purchase price of shares in Eurozet.In accordance with the provisions of the Shareholders' Agreement, with a view to protecting Agora's investment in Eurozet and protecting Agora's position as a minority shareholder of Eurozet, Agora has been granted the typical rights of a minority shareholder, including the right to appoint and dismiss one member of the Supervisory Board of Eurozet and the right to influence decisions on selected key issues concerning, in particular, the capital structure, amendment of the company deed, changes in the share capital or liquidation of the company. Agora will have these rights as long as Agora and its related entities have at least 34% plus one shares / voting rights in the share capital of Eurozet / at the Eurozet shareholders' meeting. However, Agora, as a minority shareholder, will not have influence on, among other things, the operating activities of Eurozet or the programming strategy of the radio station.

The Shareholders' Agreement also contains the following provisions governing the rules of cooperation between the shareholders, should they exit their investment in Eurozet:

- the right to demand that the second shareholder joins in the sale with respect to all its shares (`Drag Along Right'), together with the principles for securing the effective sale of the shares in relation to which the Drag Along Right has been exercised,

[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 54

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
- a shareholder's right to join in the sale of all shares held by the shareholder in the case of the sale of shares by the other shareholder (`Tag Along Right'); and - Agora's right to acquire all the remaining shares of Eurozet held by SFS Ventures (`Callable Shares') (`Call Option'), together with the principles for securing the effective acquisition of the shares in the event of exercising the Call Option.
Agora has the right (but not an obligation) to exercise the Call Option during the period commencing after the lapse of 12 months and ending after the lapse of 36 months from the date of conclusion of the Final Agreement (`Call Option Period') or until June 20, 2022, if Agora submits to SFS Ventures a declaration of will to exercise the Call Option. In specific cases described in the Shareholders' Agreement concerning a substantial reduction in the scope of the Group's core activities, the Call Option Period may be shortened. Should Agora exercise the Call Option, the purchase price of the Callable Shares for Agora will be determined on the basis of a formula set out in the Shareholders' Agreement, which takes into account SFS Ventures' achievement of certain financial indices. In accordance with the Shareholders' Agreement, Agora will be able to exercise the Call Option, and thereby take control over Eurozet, after obtaining the legally required antimonopoly permission.
Within the meaning of the Polish Accounting Act, Eurozet is an associate of Agora S.A.
The acquisition of 40% of shares in Eurozet was financed partially from the Company's own resources, and PLN 75.0 million was financed with an overdraft facility which will be converted into a non-revolving loan on the basis of a Credit Line Agreement executed on May 25, 2017 with DNB Bank Polska S.A and amended by Annex no. 1 of May 18, 2018.
On March 6, 2019, the Company received a letter from the President of the Office of Competition and Consumer Protection calling on the Company to provide information and documents as part of an investigation procedure aimed at determining whether or not an obligation to notify of an intended concentration involving the Company, SFS Ventures s.r.o. and Eurozet sp. z o.o. exists. The investigation procedure is an inquiry and is not conducted against the Company. As at the date of these financial statements the investigation procedure is pending.

Helios S.A.
Call for the repurchase of shares in a subsidiary.
On 29 March 2016, a minority shareholder ("the Minority Shareholder") of Helios S.A. holding 320,400 shares in that company, which represent 2.77% of the share capital ("the Shares"), addressed to Helios S.A. a call under Art. 418 (1) of the Code of Commercial Companies (hereinafter: "CCC") for convening the General Shareholders' Meeting and putting on its agenda passing a resolution on mandatory sell-out of the Shares ("the Call").
As a result of: (i) the Call, (ii) further calls made under Article 418(1) of the CCC by the Minority Shareholder and other minority shareholders of Helios S.A. who acquired a part of the Shares from the Minority Shareholder, and (iii) the resolutions passed by the General Shareholders' Meeting of Helios S.A. on 10 May 2016 and 13 June 2016, two sell-out procedures (under Art. 418(1) of the CCC) and one squeeze out procedure (under Article 418 of the CCC) are being finalized at Helios S.A., aimed at the acquisition by two shareholders of Helios S.A., including Agora S.A., the Shares held by the Minority Shareholder and other minority shareholders.
(i) Sell-out procedure
As part of the sell out of the Shares, by June 30, 2016, Agora transferred to Helios S.A. PLN 2,938 thousand representing the sell out price calculated in accordance with Article 418(1) para. 6 of the CCC. As at December 31, 2016, the Agora Group recognized on its balance sheet an obligation to purchase the Shares from minority shareholders of Helios S.A. totalling PLN 3,185 thousand. This included PLN 2,938 thousand already transferred by Agora S.A. to Helios S.A. (with the corresponding entry in the Group's equity under retained earnings/(accumulated losses) and the net profit or loss for the current year) and the total amount transferred by another shareholder of Helios S.A. under the sell out procedure. As part of the sell out procedure, on June 2, 2017, PLN 3,171 was transferred by Helios S.A. to the Minority Shareholder for 318,930 shares sold out. Also on June 2, 2017, a total of PLN 14 thousand was transferred to other minority shareholders for the sell out of 1,460 shares in total. As a result of these transactions, the Group fulfilled its obligation to buy shares recognized on the Group's balance sheet. As a result, Agora S.A. increased its shareholding in Helios S.A. from 10,277,800 to 10,573,352 shares, i.e. by 295,552 shares. Currently, Agora S.A. holds 91.44% of the shares in Helios S.A.
The shareholders whose shares are subject to the sell out and squeeze out procedures did not agree to the sell out share price calculated in accordance with Article 418(1) para. 6 of the CCC, and based on Article 418(1) para. 7 of the CCC submitted a motion to the registration court to appoint a registered auditor to determine the price of the shares being sold. The final price of the Shares being subject to the sell out and squeeze out procedures will be determined by the registration court competent for the registered office of Helios S.A. on the basis of an opinion of the registered auditor appointed by the registration court competent for the registered office of Helios S.A., A change in the valuation will result in an adjustment of the price of the shares being sold. The District Court for Lodz Srodmiescie in Lodz, the 20th Department of the National Court Register, appointed a registered auditor to value shares under this procedure, both for the sell out of the Minority Shareholder's shares with regard to 318,930 shares, and for other minority shareholders with regard to 1,460 shares in total.
The Minority Shareholder and other minority shareholders referred to in the preceding sentence which had rights under 1,460 shares appealed from the Court's decision appointing the registered auditor. By a valid decision of the Regional Court in Lodz, the 13th Business Appeal Department of February 20, 2019, the appeal of the other minority shareholders having rights under 1,460 shares was dismissed. To date, the appeal of the Minority Shareholder has not been considered yet.
(ii) Squeeze-out procedure
The squeeze out procedure which entered into force on July 14, 2016 is carried out with respect to 10 shares. The holder of these shares did not respond to the Company's call published in accordance with the applicable procedure in Monitor Sadowy i Gospodarczy (Court and Business Gazette) calling minority shareholders holding the said shares to submit the share documents to the Company, within two weeks of the publication of the call, under the sanction of cancelling the shares after that date. In connection with the above, on April 7, 2017, the
[ w w w . a g o r a . p l ] Page 57

Agora Group Management Discussion and Analysis for the year 2019 to the consolidated financial statements
translation only
Management Board of Helios S.A. adopted a resolution cancelling these shares and announced this in Monitor Sadowy i Gospodarczy of May 8, 2017.
Currently, the valuation of the shares by the registered auditor nominated by the Court is being finalized. As at the date of this report, the sell out and squeeze out procedures have not been completed.

In the current report of 31 January 2020, further to the regulatory filings: 4/2019 of 28 February 2019 and 10/2019 of 23 April 2019, the Management Board of Agora S.A. informs that on 31 January 2020 Helios S.A. and Step Inside sp. z o.o., Agora's subsidiaries, concluded an investment agreement (the "Investment Agreement") with some of the shareholders (the "Shareholders") of Food for Nation spólka z ograniczon odpowiedzialnoci spólka komandytowa (a limited liability company, limited partnership) and FFN.
The subject of the Investment Agreement is to define the principles of cooperation and run a joint enterprise established on the basis of Step Inside. The objective of Step Inside is to open, run and develop catering outlets with the Pasibus trademark, which will be situated mainly in shopping streets and at shopping centres.
When concluding the Investment Agreement, the Shareholders took up a total of 10% of the shares in the share capital of Step Inside (corresponding to 10% of the total number of votes at the Shareholders' Meeting), whereas Helios subsidized Step Inside with PLN 5 million. The Investment Agreement provides for the possibility of increasing the Individual Investors' interest to 40% in total, on condition that Step Inside fulfils the established financial objectives.

translation only
Previously, on the basis of a cooperation agreement with FFN of 28 February 2019 Helios S.A. subsidized Step Inside with PLN 10 million, of which Agora gave information in current report no. 4/2019 of 28 February 2019.
The Investment Agreement specifies, among other things, detailed parameters of the investors' capital investment and the mutual rights and obligations of the parties.
Yieldbird Sp. z o.o.
On August 8, 2019, Agora S.A. has concluded three share purchase agreements in a limited liability company regarding the purchase of shares in the company Yieldbird Sp. z o.o., with three shareholders of this company. 2. AGREEMENTS BETWEEN THE COMPANY AND MANAGEMENT BOARD'S MEMBERS ON COMPENSATION IN CASE OF RESIGNATION OR DISMISSAL
In accordance with binding employment contracts concluded with members of the Management Board of Agora S.A., during the period of 18 months starting the day:
on which the right of the shareholders holding series A shares to nominate candidates to the Management Board is removed from the Company's Statute; on which one entity or a group of entities acting in concert exceeds the 50% threshold of the total number of votes at the General Meeting of Shareholders of Agora S.A.; on which the Supervisory Board of the Company is appointed by voting by separate groups, should any of these contracts be terminated by the Company (Article 385 § 3-9 of the Code of Commercial Companies), the Management Board member will receive a compensation payment in the total amount being a sum of the following components: (i) the amount equivalent to 12 times the monthly basic remuneration due to the member of the Management Board of Agora S.A. for the month preceding the month in which the member of the Management Board of Agora S.A. receives the termination notice; (ii) the amount equivalent to the annual bonus for the financial year preceding the year of termination of the employment contract. The redundancy payment mentioned above shall not be due when the employment contract is terminated for reasons indicated in Article 52 § 1 of the Labour Code.
